# Ralph Progress Log
Started: Wed Jun 10 00:26:47 PDT 2026
---

## Codebase Patterns
- Backup/restore hash-chain checks (US-242): post-restore verification should
  read restored `games` + `game_events` rows and reuse
  `padrino.ops.backup_restore.verify_restored_game_hash_chain`, which converts
  `GameEvent` rows to `EventEnvelope` and delegates canonical replay to
  `export.bundle.verify_chain`. The CLI surface is `padrino game
  verify-restore <game-id> --db-url <restored-db-url>`; compare its `tip_hash`
  to the pre-backup `games.event_hash_head`.
- FAILED scheduler retry (US-241): keep persisted game-status literals in
  `padrino.db.game_status` and treat `COMPLETED` plus `FAILED` as scheduler
  terminal statuses. The benchmark scheduler retry is single-host/in-process:
  retry child executor exceptions up to `padrino_scheduler_game_max_attempts`,
  then `games_repo.mark_failed` clears `terminal_result`, stamps `completed_at`,
  and leaves ratings/read-side completed-only paths gated on `COMPLETED`.
  Regression coverage should include retry success, retry exhaustion, zero
  rating rows, no scheduler/matchmaker re-selection, and no stray `"FAILED"`
  literals outside the shared status module.
- Isolated scheduler child failures (US-240): when a gauntlet fans out child
  games, gather with `return_exceptions=True` and zip results back to the
  `_ScheduledGame` metadata so every exception carries its `game_id`. Log each
  failed child as `scheduler.game.failed` with structured `gauntlet_id`,
  `game_id`, and error fields, then let completed siblings continue through the
  normal completion/rating path. Leave durable FAILED status/retry semantics to
  the dedicated follow-up story, not the gather seam.
- Hot-path index migrations (US-239): keep Alembic index names and ORM
  `Index` declarations byte-matched, then test both the single linear head and
  a downgrade to the previous head that restores the pre-migration index set.
  For retention indexes, derive from executor predicates: completed-game scans
  use `games.completed_at IS NOT NULL` plus `is_broadcastable`, and scrub scans
  use `llm_calls.game_id` for rows where `raw_response IS NOT NULL`; partial
  indexes keep those hot rows narrow.
- Real-action NAR corpus (US-238): keep deterministic full-game goldens on
  `DeterministicMockAdapter` scripts built through the shared
  `make_role_aware_script` helper. For future role rulesets, pin
  terminal_result, event count, final event hash, and chain digest, then assert
  the role-specific event signal (`NightFeedbackDelivered`, cleaned death,
  serial kill target, jester day vote, etc.) plus replay equality. Keep
  `NoopMockAdapter` draw goldens only for legacy baseline coverage, not as proof
  that a role ruleset's NAR behavior is covered.
- Ranked lobby integrity ack (US-237): enforce
  `integrity_acknowledged` before lobby admission/cost slots are claimed, so a
  refused ranked create writes no lobby rows and burns no admission budget. Store
  the flag on the existing `Lobby` row; casual lobbies coerce it to `False`.
  Do not consume Alembic `0050` for this guard: US-239 still owns that revision,
  so the existing lobby-table migration shape carries the column and
  `test_migrations.py` asserts Alembic-upgraded DBs include it. Dashboard ranked
  creates must send the ack while keeping the request free of identity markers.
- Humans-Included leaderboard cards (US-236): expose ranked human ELO as a
  separate top-level `human_cards` read-side bucket, never inside
  `canonical_cards` or `experimental_cards`. Source it only from
  `HumanRating` rows joined through `League.kind == HUMANS_INCLUDED` and
  `League.ranked is True`, limited this wave to `GLOBAL/global`. Card
  `entity_id` is a hash of `human_player_id`; the raw `human_player_id` is never
  serialized, and the dashboard passes `humanCards` as its own section input.
- Ranked human ELO writer (US-234b): keep the Humans-Included writer separate
  from `ratings/openskill_service.py`. The terminal path first checks runtime
  `ranked`, a bound `league_id`, `League.kind == HUMANS_INCLUDED`, and
  `League.ranked is True`; only then does it call
  `ratings/human_openskill_service.update_human_ratings_for_game`. That service
  writes only `HumanRating` / `HumanRatingEvent` with `GLOBAL/global` scope this
  wave. AI seats participate as transient initial OpenSkill ratings so mixed
  human+AI games can move human principals without inserting AI rows into the
  human sibling table. Scientific ratings still fail closed through
  `_should_apply_ratings` and incomplete human-seat `agent_builds`.
- Ranked Humans-Included flag plumbing (US-234a): the Humans-Included league is
  now unique by `(ruleset_id, ranked)` via Alembic `0049`, so casual and ranked
  lobbies for the same ruleset bind distinct `League` rows. Lobby create owns
  the opt-in `ranked` flag; the human lane resolves ranked state from the
  launched `Lobby.game_id -> League` binding, stores it on `GamePersistence`,
  and passes it into `drive_game_loop`. Missing/non-HUMANS_INCLUDED bindings
  fail closed to `ranked=False`/`league_id=None`. Human seats still keep
  scientific ratings closed by incomplete `agent_builds`; ranked human ELO now
  writes through the separate US-234b sibling-table path. `0049` is consumed;
  future hot-path-index migration story US-239 must use `0050`.
- Human restart-resume tests (US-233): validate the single-host worker path by
  rehydrating from `game_events` with `rehydrate_active_human_games()`, then
  resuming through `run_human_lane` / the default human executor at the existing
  event-log head. In tests that run a real resumed game on the shared in-memory
  SQLite engine, avoid a tight human-lane heartbeat poll loop; wait on an
  executor-side event and use a long `poll_interval_s` so heartbeat writes do
  not contend with event persistence on the StaticPool connection.
- LLM cost fallback persist seam (US-232): keep
  `llm/litellm_adapter._extract_cost` response-local and returning only
  LiteLLM `_hidden_params.response_cost` or `None`. Carry the actual attempted
  LiteLLM model string on `AdapterResult.model_id`, then resolve persisted
  `LlmCall.cost_usd` in `runner/game_runner._persist_llm_call` with
  `price_turn_usd(settings, response_cost, model, input_tokens, output_tokens)`.
  Human-lane breaker/spend accounting reads the persisted row, so fallback
  pricing must be applied before `llm_calls_repo.record_call`.
- Human cost-governance cap tests (US-231): `admit_human` checks global
  inference reservation, then per-principal inference reservation, then the
  action's count cap. Count-cap tests must set the inference budget high enough
  to leave at least one `padrino_human_admission_inference_reserve_usd` slot
  after `ceil(spent_usd / reserve_usd)`, otherwise they fail earlier on
  `daily_inference_cap_reached`.
- Single-host worker liveness (US-230): for a new internal worker lane, prefer
  the existing DB-backed heartbeat ledger with a reserved worker-id prefix
  (`human-lane:`) over a new migration when the next Alembic revision is already
  allocated. Health routes must filter prefixes both ways so one lane's
  heartbeat cannot satisfy another lane's liveness probe. YAML-only compose
  shape guards that must run in the default suite should live outside
  `tests/docker/`, because that directory is auto-skipped as docker-keyworded.
- Multi-context leaderboard UI (US-229): treat `/public/leaderboard`
  `canonical_cards` / `experimental_cards` as already separated read-side
  contracts, then split canonical presentation ONLY by `scope_type`
  (`GLOBAL` vs `FACTION`) and experimental presentation ONLY by
  `context_kind` (`PLACEMENT` vs `SOLO_RATE`). Never infer faction sections
  from display names/context labels, and never co-sort cards across those
  rendered groups. Hermetic dashboard specs that navigate from home should
  intercept every `/public/*` fetch the route can trigger.
- Public leaderboard context cards (US-228): canonical cards intentionally
  include only the `GLOBAL/global` row plus every persisted `FACTION` scope for
  a CANONICAL_TEAM `RatingContext`; placement and solo cards stay in sibling
  experimental tables. Rank grouping must keep `scope_type/scope_value` in the
  group key so GLOBAL, TOWN, MAFIA, and any future faction cards never share
  rank space.
- Model rollup factions (US-227): `ratings/model_rollup.py` now treats
  persisted `Rating.scope_type == FACTION` `scope_value`s as data and exposes
  the primary aggregate as `ModelLeaderboardEntry.factions`. Keep `town` /
  `mafia` response fields only as legacy mirrors for existing consumers; new
  per-faction work should consume the faction-keyed dict and must not branch on
  exactly two factions.
- Ruleset selector metadata (US-226): public/dashboard ruleset pickers should
  consume `GET /public/rulesets` via `PadrinoClient.publicRulesets()`. The
  endpoint iterates `BUILTIN_RULESET_IDS` and resolves each with `get_ruleset`
  for `RULESET_ID`, `PLAYER_COUNT`, `RATING_CONTEXT_DISPLAY_LABEL`,
  `RATING_CONTEXT_KIND`, and `IS_CANONICAL`; do not duplicate route- or
  component-level ruleset lists.
- Spectator watch NAR outcomes (US-225): render public night deaths only from
  the projected PUBLIC `PlayerEliminated.payload.public_player_id` /
  `payload.cause`; `actor_player_id` is normally `None` for resolved
  eliminations. Do not invent a public no-death/NAR summary from
  `NightResolved`, because it is SYSTEM and dropped by spectator projection.
  Keep shared Playwright identity-blind assertions in
  `web/dashboard/tests/e2e/helpers/identityBlind.ts`.
- Server-driven play actions (US-224): the human play UI must treat
  `SeatObservationFrame.legal_actions.allowed_action_types` as the action
  universe. For night actions, select the server-provided targeted non-vote
  action and render a generic label from the action string; do not enumerate
  role/action ids in the Svelte route or `playSurface` helper.
- Frozen migration snapshots (US-223): historical migrations must not import
  live core/ruleset declarations. Seed and backfill only frozen literal rows
  that existed at the migration's ship point; newer rulesets should be
  materialized by the runtime `ensure_declared_context` path unless a future
  forward migration adds its own frozen historical backfill.
- Placement terminal resilience (US-222): keep experimental PLACEMENT rating
  writes outside the `GameTerminated` event/status transaction, and let the
  direct rating service remain strict for malformed Plackett-Luce inputs. The
  terminal path should validate winner membership against the per-game
  `seat_groups` and skip/log invalid non-faction winners, while gauntlet intake
  uses deterministic `assign_roles(derive_game_seed(...))` per clone to reject
  duplicate builds that would span placement outcome factions.
- Data-driven migration backfills (US-221): when a migration stamps historical
  rating rows from ruleset metadata, query the distinct persisted
  `SCIENTIFIC` league `ruleset_id`s and resolve each through the current
  ruleset registry's declared `RATING_CONTEXT_KIND` / `IS_CANONICAL` /
  display-label contract. Do not hardcode the sacred pair; fresh future
  scientific canonical rulesets such as `roleblock10_v1` must receive the same
  additive marker without re-rating.
- Canonicality layer-2 negative tests (US-220): to prove
  `_observed_terminal_outcomes` is not a no-op, build a minimal canonical-looking
  ruleset that passes all layer-1 flags and monkeypatch
  `rulesets.canonicality.check_win` to return deviant observed winners. This
  exercises the terminal-outcome audit directly without weakening built-in
  ruleset declarations.
- Placement terminal scoring (US-219): wire non-canonical PLACEMENT contexts
  from the runner terminal transaction, like SOLO_RATE, using
  `declared_for_ruleset` to fail closed and skipping mirror-pair games until
  paired placement scoring is defined. Derive placement groups from assigned
  seat factions, treat `DRAW` as an all-groups tie with mu frozen and sigma
  shrinking, and reject any single agent build spanning multiple placement
  outcome groups so it cannot double-count.
- Same-night-death feedback suppression (US-218): when a night role produces
  private resolved-state feedback, pass `eliminated_player_ids` into that
  feedback path and skip recipients killed that night. Apply this consistently
  for investigation-style feedback and visit-graph reads so dead observers do
  not receive post-death private state.
- Canonical full-game byte-stability (US-217): protect sacred ladders with
  runner-level golden fixtures that exercise structured night actions, not by
  asserting on NAR internals. For `mini7_v1` / `bench10_v1`, use seeded
  scripted games that include mafia kills, Doctor protects, and Detective
  investigations of every mafia seat, then pin terminal result/reason,
  eliminated sequence, event count, final event hash, and chain digest.
- Sacred canonical rulesets (US-216): never mutate an existing canonical
  ruleset roster such as `mini7_v1` or `bench10_v1` to admit a new role. Put
  new canonical role mixes behind a new `ruleset_id`, keep the old corpus
  hashes pinned, and require every built-in `IS_CANONICAL` ruleset to have a
  regression-corpus hash so future roster drift fails closed.
- Engine-stress utility roles (US-188): keep Mayor / Commuter / Mason as
  generic deterministic engine roles without admitting them to canonical
  built-in rulesets. Mayor vote weight lives in the pure day-vote resolver as
  public weighted tally metadata behind a disabled variance gate; Commuter is a
  passive NAR target bounce before visits/effects are recorded; Mason is a
  structured observation fact (`mason_partners`) keyed only by public player id,
  never a chat channel.
- Ninja visit suppression (US-187b): model Ninja as a Mafia role that uses the
  existing `MAFIA_KILL` / `FACTIONAL_KILL` path, not a new action type. Keep
  suppression at the pure NAR visit-recording seam: a Ninja factional kill
  omits only that actor's kill visit, while same-night roleblock visits remain
  visible to Tracker/Watcher. Use a dedicated canonical 10p+ ruleset
  (`ninja13_v1`) rather than mutating earlier ruleset payloads.
- Visit-graph investigative roles (US-187): keep Tracker/Watcher as pure reads
  over the NAR `VisitRecord` list. Roleblock visits are recorded at the
  roleblock tier, but a blocked actor's nullified action still does not record
  its own visit; Tracker reports the tracked actor's visited public ids and
  Watcher reports visitors to the watched public id. Ship visit-graph roles in
  a dedicated canonical 10p+ ruleset (`visit12_v1`) rather than changing older
  legacy ruleset payloads.
- Multi-context public presentation (US-186): keep public rating cards as a
  read-side contract, not a write path. Query canonical cards only through the
  scientific `Rating` rows with a canonical `RatingContext`; query
  experimental cards only from the sibling `placement_ratings` /
  `solo_rate_ratings` tables. Return `canonical_cards` and
  `experimental_cards` as separate arrays, assign ranks only within exact
  `(context_kind, ruleset_id, scope_type, scope_value, metric)` groups, and
  set provisional cards' `rank` to `None` even if their raw score is higher.
- SOLO_RATE alt-win roles (US-185): model the objective as a pure
  `ALT_TRIGGER` win condition on a non-canonical ruleset, fold the trigger from
  structured mechanical events (Jester: `PlayerEliminated` with `role=JESTER`
  and day-vote cause), and have the runner write one role-scoped
  `SoloRateAttempt` from terminal state. Do not parse chat, do not expose
  model/build identity in the signal, and keep canonical/placement paths
  returning zero rows.
- SOLO_RATE scoring (US-184): keep alt-win / orthogonal solo objectives out of
  every team-ELO path. Resolve only an explicit non-canonical `SOLO_RATE`
  context, write success/attempt counts to `solo_rate_ratings` /
  `solo_rate_rating_events`, and expose read-side cards only after a
  minimum-attempt gate with Beta-posterior credible intervals.
- Solo-faction placement rulesets (US-183): keep solo / three-faction variants
  non-canonical with `RATING_CONTEXT_KIND = PLACEMENT` and an explicit
  `SOLO_FACTIONS` declaration. Model terminal logic with ordered
  `WIN_CONDITIONS`: Town eliminates every threat faction, solo wins through
  `SOLO_LAST_ALIVE`, and Mafia parity is blocked by the live solo faction.
  Independent solo kills should be first-class NAR actions that populate
  `MatrixNightResolution.eliminated_player_ids`, while legacy `eliminated`
  remains the first deterministic death for older callers. Add every new
  runner-emitted submission event to `diagnostics/submissions.py`.
- Non-canonical placement scoring (US-182): keep PLACEMENT OpenSkill writes on
  the sibling `placement_ratings` / `placement_rating_events` tables keyed by
  `rating_context_id`; do not accept a `league_id` or touch canonical
  `Rating` / `RatingEvent`. Resolve only an explicit non-canonical PLACEMENT
  context for the game's ruleset, rank the winner's terminal group first, and
  tie every other terminal group for second.
- Submission diagnostics vocabulary (US-181): keep timeout/invalid-rate
  denominators in one read-side constant set (`diagnostics/submissions.py`) and
  include every runner-emitted structured submission event plus failure events.
  When adding a role event such as `TrackSubmitted`, update that vocabulary so
  gauntlet, league, and model diagnostics keep the same denominator across
  rulesets and ladders.
- Mirror-paired canonical ratings (US-180): persist paired benchmark legs as
  distinct `games` rows sharing `pair_id`, with `pair_leg=0` using roster order
  and `pair_leg=1` using the mirrored roster while preserving the same
  `game_seed`. Runner scheduling must compute `agent_builds_by_seat` per game,
  not per gauntlet. Pair rating should canonicalize by `(game_seed, pair_leg,
  game_id)` and apply both legs in one transaction; a completed-pair recovery
  pass after gauntlet execution should be idempotent so close-finishing legs
  cannot leave an unrated pair.
- Variance-gated active roles (US-178): implement deterministic mechanics in
  pure NAR first, but keep canonical inclusion behind a pure numeric gate
  module with explicit sample and variance thresholds. Until the gate has the
  required measured mirror-pair sample, built-in canonical rulesets should stay
  role-free and future rulesets can conditionally include the role by reading
  that gate. Limited-use active roles should spend shots from hidden
  post-resolution event payload fields, not from submission events.
- Limited-use NAR actions (US-177): if an active night role has a per-game
  shot cap, do not spend it from the submission event because the runner folds
  submissions before phase resolution. Emit the successful spend on a hidden
  post-resolution event (`NightResolved.clean_spent_actor_ids`) and fold that
  field in the reducer, while omitting empty fields from runner event bodies to
  preserve legacy corpus hashes.
- Role-gated active NAR roles (US-176): keep action eligibility enforced in
  both `legal_actions_for` and the NAR target validator; runner-submitted raw
  intents must not let arbitrary actors use future active night actions. New
  dedicated canonical rulesets should register through `get_ruleset` and
  `BUILTIN_RULESET_IDS`, while preserving existing legacy corpus hashes unless
  the older ruleset payload itself intentionally changes.
- Passive investigation falsifiers (US-175): keep the role passive at the NAR
  finding seam (`core/engine/resolvers/nar.py::_finding_for`) so both the legacy
  Detective helper and full night resolver share the same structured feedback.
  If the role still participates in the factional kill, add it to the narrow
  factional-kill role set in `legal_actions_for` rather than granting broad
  Mafia-faction kill actions to future active scum roles.
- Generalized terminal policy substrate (US-215): `core/engine/win_conditions.py` owns the ordered `WinCondition` policy tuple. Existing two-faction rulesets should declare `WIN_CONDITIONS = canonical_two_faction_win_conditions()` so `TOWN` / `MAFIA` / `DRAW` payloads and hashes stay byte-stable. Non-canonical rulesets can add `TARGET_FACTIONS_ELIMINATED`, `FACTION_PARITY` with `blocked_by_alive_factions`, `SOLO_LAST_ALIVE`, and `ALT_TRIGGER` policies, but canonical ratings remain gated separately on exact `TOWN|MAFIA|DRAW` winners. Store future alt-win facts as pure state triggers, not by parsing chat.
- Structured night-action vocabulary is a three-layer contract (US-214): add the public `ActionType`, the matrix `NightActionKind`/`ResolutionMatrixRow`, and the runner/event-log submission event together. `legal_actions_for` remains the only producer of per-seat action availability, while `action_requires_target(...)` is the shared target-validation helper for runner coercion, the human adapter, and the human POST channel. Global `Role` enum membership is now future-ready; code that needs the roles in a concrete ruleset must iterate that ruleset's `ROLE_COUNTS`, not `for role in Role`.
- NAR matrix as the only night-interaction seam (US-174): add future night roles by adding a `NightActionKind` + `ResolutionMatrixRow` in `core/engine/resolvers/nar.py`, then translating structured submissions into `NightActionIntent`s. Keep the old `mafia_kill` / `doctor_protect` / `detective` modules as compatibility wrappers only; runner-facing `resolve_night` should route through `resolve_current_night`. Pinned rules: roleblock-vs-roleblock applies both blocks, a roleblocked sole factional killer does not get an automatic backup carry, blocked active actions do not record visits, and investigations of targets killed that night still resolve if the investigator survives.
- Draw-safe canonical OpenSkill updates (US-173): canonical `DRAW` outcomes still run through the equal-rank OpenSkill path to shrink sigma, but the persisted `mu` is frozen at the pre-draw value for every scope row. This prevents a day-cap/draw meta from farming `mu`; any conservative-score movement after a draw is only uncertainty shrinkage. Per-role sample diagnostics should stay read-side over `game_seats` and exact `Role` values, while Town/Mafia Elo diagnostics come from existing `FACTION` scope rows.
- Canonical ruleset purity is a pure-core contract (US-172): `core/rulesets/canonicality.py` is the single validator for CANONICAL_TEAM eligibility. A canonical ruleset must explicitly declare no `ALT_WIN_CONDITIONS`, `SOLO_FACTIONS`, `FACTION_MUTATION_ALLOWED`, or `KINGMAKING_OBJECTIVE`; the validator enumerates alive Town/Mafia count states through `check_win` and requires ranked outcomes exactly `{TOWN, MAFIA}` with `DRAW` mapping to equal team ranks. Keep OpenSkill rank mapping wired through `canonical_team_ranks_for_outcome(...)` so draw/tie semantics cannot drift from the gate.
- Rating contexts compose with, not replace, the League.kind firewall (US-171): keep canonical OpenSkill writes on the existing `Rating` / `RatingEvent` reach path (`League.kind == SCIENTIFIC` plus the runner/rating-service fail-closed chokepoints), and use `rating_context_id` only as additive metadata on those rows. Resolve a CANONICAL_TEAM context by checking BOTH the ruleset declaration (`RATING_CONTEXT_KIND == CANONICAL_TEAM` and `IS_CANONICAL`) and the persisted `rating_contexts` row (`is_canonical=True`); any missing/unknown/non-canonical context returns no writes. Non-canonical contexts get sibling tables (`placement_*`, `solo_rate_*`) and must never touch the sacred canonical tables.
- Retryable security-ledger claims need explicit failure classification (US-213): when a durable single-use claim is committed before a downstream exchange, default failures should remain terminal/burned, and only explicitly transient infrastructure failures should release the claim in a separate committed transaction. Carry both an `error_class` and `transient` flag on the domain error, map live network/5xx/provider-temporary errors to transient, keep `invalid_grant` terminal, and regression-test retry success after transient release plus replay rejection after terminal failure.
- Validate committed event re-seals before recovery side effects (US-212): in crash-recovery paths that mirror a durable `StoredEvent` into long-lived memory, compute `compute_event_hash(event.prev_event_hash, event.body)` and compare it to the committed `event.event_hash` before mutating auxiliary in-memory state such as mux dispatch tables or appending to `EventLog`. Keep the later append/hash assertion as a guard, but the primary corrupt-row rejection must be pre-mutation so the error path leaves memory untouched.
- Post-commit recovery must distinguish memory lag from identity desync (US-211): a force-sync path may repair a known in-memory mirror that lagged after a durable commit, but it must not invent a new identity key. For takeover recovery, expose a mux membership predicate (`has_seat`) and reject unknown seats with `TakeoverApplyRecoveryError` before `force_swap_seat`, then regression-test both the unknown-seat desync and the known-seat US-206 resync path.
- Atomic multi-bucket rate limiting (US-210): when one user-visible request consumes several buckets, keep `peek_request` only as a read-only fast reject and use `RateLimitStore.record_requests([...])` for the authoritative commit. The database backend must upsert all touched buckets inside one transaction and roll the whole transaction back if any bucket exceeds its limit, so a late game/phase 429 cannot burn the broader per-principal bucket. Regression-test the TOCTOU window with a wrapper that fills the narrow bucket after its peek admits, then assert the rejected request leaves the broad bucket unchanged for every channel.
- Hot-path security-ledger cleanup should be sampled or scheduled, not unconditional (US-209): if a ledger row is short-lived garbage and stale rows are inert (OAuth consumed-flow rows are keyed by fresh per-start random `flow` tokens), do the security-critical claim on every request but run the sweep only on a stable sample such as `sha256(flow) % N == 0`. Keep the sweep in a short durable transaction when it does run, index the sweep predicate column (`consumed_at`), and test both branches by monkeypatching the sample predicate rather than depending on random token generation.
- Durable security ledgers must commit outside the request transaction when their contract says "attempted means spent" (US-208): a request-scoped `get_session` rolls back on any later exception, so an OAuth single-use flow claim written there disappears if provider exchange/account/session creation fails. Use a fresh `session_factory()` transaction for the ledger claim, commit it before the external/downstream step, then keep ordinary account/session writes in the request transaction. Regression-test by forcing the downstream step to raise, replaying the same signed state/code, and asserting the ledger row persists and the replay is rejected.
- Optional numeric Settings that are operator-disableable need an explicit env parsing seam (US-207): `int | None` fields work for Python construction, but pydantic-settings does not parse env strings like `"none"`/`"null"` as `None` by default. Add a narrow `@field_validator(..., mode="before")` on that field rather than changing global settings parsing. Then test default, numeric override, and env `none` so the escape hatch works in deployment config.
- Post-commit in-memory mirrors need a recovery path (US-206): when the DB commits an event row before the long-lived in-memory state applies the paired change, wrap the post-commit apply. If it fails, first verify the committed `StoredEvent` still matches the in-memory chain: if the exact event is already present, treat it as synced; if it is the next contiguous event with the current head hash, append its body and assert the hash matches; otherwise raise a dedicated fatal recovery error before building another event at the colliding sequence. Then force the side-effect mirror (for takeover, the mux seat binding) to match the committed row. Regression-test by monkeypatching the post-commit apply to raise, then persisting one more event at the next sequence to prove there is no `game_events` collision.
- Dedup migrations must resolve child-table unique scopes before FK repointing (US-205): when collapsing duplicate parent rows, a blind `UPDATE child SET parent_id=:keeper WHERE parent_id=:loser` can collide if the child table has a UNIQUE key that includes `parent_id`. For tables like `ratings(league_id, agent_build_id, scope_type, scope_value)` and `human_rating(league_id, human_player_id, scope_type, scope_value)`, first DELETE loser rows whose remaining scope tuple already exists under the keeper, then repoint the non-colliding survivor rows. Keep plain repointing for child tables whose uniqueness is not parent-scoped (e.g. event audit rows keyed by `game_id`) and for tables with no relevant unique scope. Regression-test by upgrading to the previous revision, seeding both a colliding loser row and a non-colliding loser survivor, then upgrading through the target migration and asserting the keeper row survives, the colliding loser row is gone, and the survivor is repointed.
- Peek-then-commit still has an atomic commit decision (US-204): `peek_request` is only a non-mutating preflight to avoid the common multi-bucket budget-burn path. Under concurrent `DatabaseRateLimitStore` callers, several requests can all peek-pass at count==limit-1, so the SECOND loop must capture every `record_request(...)` result and raise the channel's 429 when `allowed=False`; never discard the authoritative atomic increment-and-check decision. Regression-test this deterministically with a small barrier wrapper around `DatabaseRateLimitStore` that waits until all same-principal peeks finish before allowing commits, then assert only one of K requests admits when the bucket was preseeded to limit-1. Keep the existing InMemory tests that prove a peek-rejected per-game/phase bucket does not increment the per-principal bucket.
- Peek-then-commit for multi-bucket rate limiting (US-203): when one request must clear SEVERAL `RateLimitStore` buckets (e.g. per-principal AND per-game/phase in `human_actions.py` / `human_chat.py`), do NOT call `record_request` per bucket in a loop — it INCREMENTS before returning a decision, so a later bucket's 429 has already burned the earlier bucket's slot. Add a non-incrementing `peek_request(key_hash, now=, limit_per_minute=, window_seconds=)` to the `RateLimitStore` Protocol (`api/rate_limit_store.py`) and BOTH backends: `InMemoryRateLimitStore` reads the current-window count and returns allowed/retry_after without writing; `DatabaseRateLimitStore` does a plain `SELECT count` for the `(key_hash, window_start)` row (NO upsert, NO eviction). Enforcement = peek EVERY bucket first, and only if all admit, `record_request` ALL of them (all-or-nothing). A peek-time rejection by any bucket raises 429 carrying that bucket's `retry_after_seconds`; no bucket is committed on that preflight-rejected request. Test it at the helper level by inspecting `store._counts` (InMemory) after a forced-rejection request: the earlier bucket count must be unchanged. Use `pytest.raises(HTTPException)` (NOT blind `Exception` — ruff B017) and assert `exc_info.value.status_code == 429`.
- Tolerate core 'num/den' fraction-strings in dashboard percentage formatters (US-203): `core/turing/scoring.py _accuracy_string` can emit a reduced ratio like '2/3' (repeating decimals), and `Number('2/3')` is NaN — so a naive `pct()` em-dashes it. A robust `pct()` (web/dashboard `profile/+page.svelte`) parses `^(-?\d+)\/(\d+)$` into a percentage, still handles numeric + decimal-string inputs, and falls back to rendering the string VERBATIM (mirrors the reveal-page fix) for any non-empty unparseable value rather than an em-dash (empty string still em-dashes). The `detection_accuracy` field is typed `string` in `lib/api/types.ts`.
- Server-side single-use ledger for OAuth flow replay (US-202, corrected by US-208): OAuth `state`/`nonce` are stateless signed tokens with no inherent single-use guarantee, so within the 600s flow-cookie TTL the same `(state cookie, code)` pair could mint a SECOND session — the only block was the upstream provider invalidating the auth code on first redemption (provider-dependent). FIX = a tiny short-TTL table `oauth_consumed_flows(flow PK, consumed_at)` (migration `0046`, down_revision `0045`) keyed on the per-flow random `flow` token already minted in `oauth._encode_state` (`generate_token(32)` baked into the SIGNED state payload). Expose `oauth.state_flow_token(config, state)` that RE-VERIFIES the state signature via `_decode_state` (so a forged state can't inject an attacker-chosen flow key) and returns the `flow` claim. Repo `oauth_consumed_flows.try_consume_flow(session, flow=, consumed_at=)` does a dialect-aware `INSERT ... ON CONFLICT (flow) DO NOTHING ... RETURNING flow` and returns `result.scalar_one_or_none() is not None` (True only if THIS call inserted; the mirror of the heartbeat upsert but DO NOTHING not DO UPDATE). The callback (routes/human.py) calls `_try_consume_oauth_flow_durably(...)` AFTER signature/binding validation and BEFORE `exchange_code`; that helper uses a fresh `session_factory()` session, prunes expired rows, inserts-or-rejects the flow, and COMMITS before provider exchange so later callback rollback cannot erase the single-use claim. A False result raises `HTTPException(400, "oauth_state_replayed")` fail-closed. mypy: `result.rowcount` lives on `CursorResult` not `Result`, so `assert isinstance(result, CursorResult)` (import from `sqlalchemy.engine`) before reading `rowcount` in `prune_expired`. New model `OAuthConsumedFlow` goes in `db/models.py` + `__all__` (alphabetical: after `ModelProvider`, before `OAuthIdentity`). Migration test (`test_migrations_all_dialects`) uses a SUBSET check so a new table needs no EXPECTED_TABLES edit. Replay e2e test GOTCHA: the FIRST successful callback persists a `HUMAN_SESSION_COOKIE` on the httpx client jar, so the second request would compute a DIFFERENT `oauth_session_binding` and 400 with `oauth_state_mismatch` (not `oauth_state_replayed`) — call `client.cookies.clear()` between the two callbacks so the replay carries the IDENTICAL binding context and the single-use store is provably the rejecter. A distinct fresh `/start` mints a new flow token, so a second legitimate login is never blocked (only an exact replay is).
- OAuth hardening: fail-closed dedicated state key + azp + iat max-age via an impure clock seam (US-201). (a) FAIL-CLOSED state key: when a secret-derived fallback is "reconstructable from another secret an attacker may hold", deleting the derivation is not enough — make the dedicated key REQUIRED. `_resolve_state_signing_key` now returns `str | None` (the explicit `padrino_oauth_state_signing_key` or None) and is folded into `resolve_oauth_config`'s `required` tuple with the other credentials so an unset/blank key yields `None` config => the routes 503 (no usable OAuth). mypy can't narrow `state_signing_key` through `any(v is None for v in required)`, so add an explicit `assert state_signing_key is not None` next to the other `assert ... is not None` lines before constructing `OAuthConfig`. The non-derivability TEST must recompute the OLD derivation `base64url(HMAC(client_secret, b"padrino.oauth.state-signing-key.v1"))` and assert the resolved key != that (byte-inequality-vs-client_secret alone is too weak). Because the test env now needs the key, ADD `PADRINO_OAUTH_STATE_SIGNING_KEY` to the shared `_OAUTH_ENV` fixture dict — otherwise every existing OAuth test 503s. (b) azp: authlib's `validate_aud` accepts a token whose `aud` merely CONTAINS `client_id`, so a token minted for another RP (`aud=[client_id, other-rp]`, `azp=other-rp`) validates. Enforce OIDC manually AFTER `claims.validate()`: `if (aud_is_multi or azp is not None) and azp != client_id: raise` (single combined `if`, ruff SIM102). (c) iat max-age: authlib only rejects FUTURE-dating, never an upper age bound. Add a module-level impure clock seam `_NOW: Callable[[], float] = time.time` with `set_clock`/`reset_clock` (api lane, pure-core firewall N/A) and reject when `_NOW() - iat > MAX_AGE + LEEWAY`. Test the stale-but-unexpired case by signing `iat=now-4000, exp=now+1e6` and `set_clock(lambda: now)` so authlib's own exp/iat checks pass on the real clock while the max-age check fires; reset the clock in an autouse teardown fixture.
- Monotonic ON-CONFLICT upsert + revalidate-under-lock for last-seen-wins races (US-200): an `INSERT ... ON CONFLICT DO UPDATE` whose `set_` is unconditional is LAST-COMMITTER-WINS regardless of timestamp — an out-of-order older write (a delayed heartbeat, or a stale `mark_disconnected` racing a newer reconnect) clobbers the fresher row. Make it MONOTONIC by guarding the conflict update with `where=excluded.updated_at >= Model.updated_at` (an older write becomes a NO-OP, not an error) AND setting the high-water column via `GREATEST` (pg) / `MAX` (sqlite) wrapped in `coalesce(Model.col, excluded.col)` so a NULL existing value doesn't poison the comparison. Keep both dialect branches with DISTINCTLY-NAMED locals (`pg_ins`/`sqlite_ins`, `pg_update: dict[str, Any]`/`sqlite_update`) or mypy fires `Incompatible types in assignment` on the shared `stmt`/`ins` variable (the two dialect Insert types are unrelated). The no-op branch must NOT assert THIS call wrote — re-read and return the current (possibly fresher) row. SEPARATELY, when a worker reads a presence/state row to decide an irreversible flip (seat takeover), a plain unlocked SELECT under READ COMMITTED can't see a row a reconnect commits in the read->commit window: take the row `FOR UPDATE` (add a `for_update: bool=False` kwarg to the repo `get` that appends `.with_for_update()`; portable no-op on SQLite single-writer) and RE-EVALUATE the grace/expiry predicate AFTER acquiring the lock. Regression-test the window by monkeypatching the repo `get` (patch the imported module object, which `human_lane` shares — do NOT reference `human_lane.presence_repo` as the monkeypatch target or mypy errors "does not explicitly export attribute") to commit a reconnect heartbeat in its OWN session the FIRST time `for_update=True` is passed, then assert the takeover is cancelled. Prove the lock is load-bearing by flipping `for_update=False` in source: the test must fail.
- A migration that adds a UNIQUE constraint/index must DEDUP existing rows first (US-199): if the pre-migration code path created rows with no DB constraint, a deployed DB can already violate the new uniqueness — and `op.create_index(..., unique=True)` (or a unique constraint) will raise a duplicate-key IntegrityError and ABORT the upgrade. Run an in-place dedup in `upgrade()` BEFORE the index: `bind = op.get_bind()`, SELECT the candidate rows, group by the to-be-unique key, keep the earliest `(created_at, id)` keeper, REPOINT every dependent FK to the keeper, then DELETE the losers. Repoint across ALL tables with a FK to the parent (grep `ForeignKey("<table>.id")` in models.py) via a fixed allowlist of `(table, column)` tuples, each guarded by `sa.inspect(bind).has_table(table)` so the same revision is safe regardless of which sibling tables exist at run time. Use portable raw `sa.text` UPDATE/DELETE so it runs identically on SQLite + Postgres. If a story says the migration is part of THIS unmerged wave, fold the dedup into that revision IN PLACE — do NOT add a new revision (keeps the chain linear, head unchanged). Regression-test: `command.upgrade(cfg, "<prev>")`, seed duplicates + a dependent row pointing at the LOSER, then `command.upgrade(cfg, "<this>")` MUST NOT raise; assert one row per key, earliest keeper survived, dependent repointed, index exists. GOTCHA: SQLite stores `sa.Uuid` as 32-char hex, so raw-SQL seeds/asserts must bind/compare on `uuid.uuid4().hex` — binding a `uuid.UUID` object raises `sqlite3.ProgrammingError: type 'UUID' is not supported`.
- Admission slot lifecycle around launch — bind on created, release on charged-accounting takeover (US-198): the `POST /lobbies/{id}/launch` handler called `_enforce_admission(action=ACTION_LAUNCH)` but DISCARDED the `HumanAdmitDecision`, so the GAME-bucket `HumanCostAdmission` count slot + the GLOBAL+per-user `HumanInferenceReservation` rows it claimed stayed `lobby_id=NULL` forever (never releasable, LIVE the whole `reservation_day`). Two compounding leaks: (1) admission ran BEFORE `launch_lobby`'s idempotency short-circuit, so every re-launch leaked another set (self-DoS); (2) launch's GAME-bucket count slot DOUBLE-COUNTED with create's (both share `_admission_bucket(...)=="game"`), and the host's OWN create slot then BLOCKED their launch at `games_per_day=1`. THREE-PART FIX in the route: (a) short-circuit the already-LAUNCHED case (`lobby.status==LAUNCHED and game_id is not None`) BEFORE `_enforce_admission`, mirroring join_lobby's existing-member guard — an idempotent re-launch claims nothing; (b) `release_admission_for_lobby(lobby_id)` the create-time slots BEFORE launch admission so the host's own create slot can't block their launch, then bind launch's count slot via `bind_admission_slots(decision, lobby_id=, lobby_member_id=host_member.id)` on `result.created` — the materialized game now counts via `_principal_games_today` (legacy implicit), so exactly ONE live GAME `HumanCostAdmission` slot remains; (c) on `result.created` also call the NEW `release_inference_reservations_for_lobby(lobby_id)` so HELD `HumanInferenceReservation` rows are released and charged `LlmCall` spend (`_implicit_budget_used = ceil(spent/reserve)`) becomes the SOLE inference-$ accounting — held reservation + charged spend never count the same dollars twice (without this a user hit `daily_inference_cap_reached` at ~HALF the real $ cap). A failed launch (`LobbyNotLaunchableError`/`AutoFillPoolError`) or a `created=False` race calls the NEW `rollback_admission_decision(decision)` which HARD-DELETEs (not releases — never bound) the freshly claimed count slot + reservations. Two new governance helpers added to `human_cost_governance.py` + `__all__`: `release_inference_reservations_for_lobby` (releases ONLY inference rows for a lobby, leaves the count slot) and `rollback_admission_decision` (deletes a decision's slots by id). Regression-test at the REAL endpoints with pinned `Settings` (reserve_usd=0.5, inference cap=5.0 => 10 slots): launch N games charging real $1.0 LlmCall each, assert a new create still admits below the cap and only denies once CHARGED spend reaches it (proves no double-count); plus `games_per_day=1` create+launch succeeds and a 2nd create denies; plus two launches leave exactly ONE live `bucket="game"` `HumanCostAdmission`.
- Apply irreversible in-memory mutations only AFTER the paired DB commit (US-197): the takeover did two un-rollbackable in-memory writes (`mux.swap_seat` in-place dict write + `event_log.append`) BEFORE `_persist_stored_event_row` inside the takeover `session.begin()`. The mux/event_log/state are LONG-LIVED objects reused across ticks, so a flush/commit failure (deadlock, serialization, `uq_game_event_sequence` collision) rolled back the DB but left the in-memory log/mux advanced past what is durable -> later `persist_pending_events` re-inserts the orphan AND the DB-only recheck re-takes the seat (second SeatTakenOver, hash-chain corruption). FIX = split `disconnect_takeover.take_over_seat` into a PURE `build_takeover_event(...)` (computes the sealed `StoredEvent` from `event_log.head_hash`+`len(events)` WITHOUT appending) and an in-memory-commit `apply_takeover(...)` (validates the event still seals onto the current head, then `swap_seat`+`event_log.append`). The lane now: build envelope -> `_persist_stored_event_row` + seat mutation inside `session.begin()` (commit) -> ONLY THEN `apply_takeover`. If the commit raises, control never reaches `apply_takeover`, so the mux still routes the seat to the HUMAN adapter and the log has no orphan (apply-after-commit > revert-on-failure: no compensating swap-back needed). `take_over_seat` kept as a build+apply wrapper so the unit tests (test_disconnect_takeover.py) and the unknown-seat KeyError path are unchanged. Belt-and-suspenders recheck (`_seat_has_in_memory_takeover(event_log, seat_id)`) scans the in-memory log for an existing SeatTakenOver for the seat and skips, so a retry never double-appends even if the DB seat reads stale. Regression: monkeypatch `human_lane._persist_stored_event_row` to raise (stands in for any in-txn flush/commit failure), assert the mux seat is still a `HumanAdapter` + zero SeatTakenOver in-memory/DB + seat still HUMAN; then `monkeypatch.undo()` and re-run -> exactly one takeover, one persisted row, one contiguous new sequence.
- Co-commit LOWER in-memory failure events in the chat-release txn, not just the chat row (US-196, extends US-189): US-189 co-committed the HIGHER content_ref chat row (sequence N+1) with the sidecar/hold write but left the LOWER `ActionTimedOut`/`OutputInvalid` failure events (sequence N) — appended to the in-memory `event_log` earlier in the SAME human tick — to be mirrored only by the post-tick `persist_pending_events(log_before)` (game_runner.py:867). A crash after the N+1 commit but before that persist left `game_events` holding `{N-1, N+1}` with N missing -> `replay_event_log` re-seals non-contiguously and raises `ReplayHashMismatchError` on rehydrate (the game can never resume). FIX: thread the not-yet-persisted lower events into `release_held_chat_for_phase(..., pending_lower_events=...)` and persist them in the SAME `session.begin()` BEFORE the chat row. `_run_human_tick_responses` records `log_before = len(event_log.events)` BEFORE `run_human_tick`, then hands `event_log.events[log_before:]` (the failure rows the tick appended) to the `release_chat` callable. The helper skips any already-persisted sequence via `events_repo.persisted_sequences_from(session, game_id, from_sequence=min(pending))` so a partial prior `persist_pending_events` retry never re-inserts (no `uq_game_event_sequence` collision). `HumanChatRelease` type alias gained a 4th `Sequence[StoredEvent]` param — every test closure passing a `release_chat` to `_run_human_tick_responses` (test_invariants_human_mp / test_human_lane_wiring / integration/test_human_game_e2e) must add+forward it. Regression-test the gap WITHOUT calling persist: seed sequence N-1 in `game_events`, append a failure event at N to the in-memory log only, call release with `pending_lower_events=(failure,)`, then assert `replay_state_from_rows(list_events(...))` succeeds over a contiguous chain. NOTE the failure-event body must satisfy its pydantic payload schema (`OutputInvalidPayload` needs both `reason` AND `validation_errors`) or `replay_state_from_rows` -> `EventAdapter.validate_python` raises during rehydrate.
- Shared seat-auth + partial-unique idempotent get_or_create (US-195): the human-lane seat-auth source of truth is `api/human_seat_auth.resolve_human_game_seat(...)`. It takes an optional `restrict_to_human_lane: bool = False` that, when set, AND-filters `seat_kind IN HUMAN_LANE_SEAT_KINDS` — use `restrict_to_human_lane=True` on identity-disclosure surfaces (the reveal route) so an upstream invariant break can never widen the principal->seat binding. Do NOT re-define a private seat-auth resolver per route (the reveal route's old `resolve_participant_seat` drifted; it was deleted). For dormant singleton rows scoped by a key (the HUMANS_INCLUDED league per ruleset), enforce a PARTIAL unique index (`leagues (kind, ruleset_id) WHERE kind = 'HUMANS_INCLUDED'`, migration `0045`, sqlite+pg portable) AND make get_or_create race-idempotent with a `session.begin_nested()` SAVEPOINT around the conflicting `flush()`: on `IntegrityError`, roll back to the savepoint and re-read the winner's row — this avoids poisoning the caller's outer transaction (a bare flush failure aborts the whole txn). Type the inner `select` helper as `Select[tuple[Model]]` (NOT `Any`) or mypy `no-any-return` fires when its `.scalar_one_or_none()` result is returned as the declared model type. Reuse one runtime read via `ResolvedHumanState.runtime`; the reveal non-terminal 409 path uses cache-backed `resolve_current_human_state` not a full event-log replay. Frontend: render server-formatted accuracy (now a fraction STRING like '2/3', not a decimal) verbatim — NO `parseFloat` (would NaN); the dashboard pins this with a `reveal-accuracy-value` testid + an e2e case asserting exact text '2/3' and not 'NaN'.
- State-cache tamper detection + tri-state upsert (US-194): the US-168 human request fast path resolves `(GameState, EventLog)` from the durable `human_game_runtime.state_cache` instead of a full event-log re-fold. The integrity hole: `EventLog.from_stored(...)` PRESERVED the cached envelopes' stored `event_hash` WITHOUT recomputing it from the body (only contiguity + `prev_event_hash` pointers were checked), and `resolve_current_human_state` only cross-checks the CACHED HEAD's hash against the DB head row — so a tampered PRE-HEAD body in the cache (head hash left intact) was served, weakening the tamper detection the old `replay_state_from_rows` (full re-seal via `replay_event_log`) gave. FIX: `from_stored` now recomputes `compute_event_hash(prev_hash, stored.body)` per event and raises `ValueError` on any body/hash mismatch (full re-seal, same guarantee as replay; `compute_event_hash` was already imported so NO new core dependency / no circular import with `replay.py`). `_parse_state_cache` already catches `ValueError`->None so a tampered cache falls back to the verified full DB replay (returns `used_cache=False`) — correctness preserved, never silently served. Complete cache adoption: `api/human_turing.py::submit_guess` switched from `replay_state_from_rows(rows)` to the shared `resolve_current_human_state(session, game_id)` (None->404; one state-resolution path across action/chat/observation/turing). Tri-state upsert: `db/repositories/human_game_runtime.upsert` `state_cache` param default is now a private `_Unset` enum sentinel (NOT None — None is a real "clear the cache" value): OMITTED preserves an existing cache (insert defaults to None), a dict REPLACES, explicit None CLEARS. This stops a future partial-update caller that doesn't manage the cache from silently wiping it; the existing `human_lane.py` snapshotter still passes `state_cache=...` explicitly so its behavior is unchanged. Tests: `tests/core/test_event_log.py` (from_stored round-trips, detects tampered pre-head body whose stored hash is intact, rejects broken pointer); `tests/runner/test_human_state_cache_integrity.py` (tamper a pre-head `assignments[0].role` in the cache JSON -> resolve falls back with `used_cache=False`; omit->preserve, explicit None->clear).
- OAuth id_token lifetime hardening + dedicated state key (US-193): authlib's `claims.validate()` only checks `exp`/`iat` WHEN PRESENT, so a signature-valid id_token with NO `exp` claim was accepted as a permanent login. Fix: mark `exp` AND `iat` as `{"essential": True}` in the `claims_options` passed to `jwt.decode(...)` (verified: an exp-less token then raises `MissingClaimError`, fail-closed) and call `claims.validate(leeway=_CLAIMS_LEEWAY_SECONDS)` (60s skew tolerance; authlib's `validate_iat` rejects an `iat` too far in the future, `validate_exp` rejects past `exp`). Separately, the CSRF/session-binding state HMAC was keyed on `config.client_secret`; added `OAuthConfig.state_signing_key` resolved by `_resolve_state_signing_key(settings)` = the new optional `padrino_oauth_state_signing_key` verbatim if set, else a DOMAIN-SEPARATED HMAC of the client secret (`hmac(client_secret, b"padrino.oauth.state-signing-key.v1")`, base64url) so the state key is never EQUAL to the client secret (leaked-secret blast radius narrowed) yet the flow needs no extra deploy config. `_state_signature` now uses `config.state_signing_key`. Test seam: the existing `_signed_id_token(...)` test helper gained `exp`/`include_exp` params; a parametrized test that spreads `**claims` into it must annotate `claims: dict[str, Any]` (mixed value types vs the int/bool kwargs).
- Race-safe presence upsert (US-192): `db/repositories/human_seat_presence.py` `record_heartbeat` / `mark_disconnected` no longer read-then-insert (which raced two concurrent first heartbeats into both INSERTing and the second violating `uq_human_seat_presence` -> 500). Both now route through `_upsert_presence(...)`, a dialect-aware `INSERT ... ON CONFLICT (game_id, public_player_id) DO UPDATE` (pg + sqlite branches, same shape as the chat sidecar counter). KEY gotchas for a Core upsert vs ORM insert: (1) ORM column defaults (`id=uuid4`, `updated_at=onupdate`) do NOT fire on a Core `insert()`, so supply EVERY column explicitly in `.values()`; (2) a Core upsert bypasses the ORM identity map, so any instance already loaded for that key is stale — `get(...)` then `session.expire(existing)` then re-`get(...)` so the returned ORM row reflects what was written. `mark_disconnected` uses a `_KEEP` sentinel (None is a real value) to NOT touch `last_seen_at` on UPDATE (preserve the last live heartbeat for grace-window measurement) but set it None on INSERT — matching the pre-existing semantics. Concurrency test pattern: file-based sqlite engine + `create_session_factory`, an `asyncio.Event` barrier, N tasks each in their OWN `session_factory()` + `session.begin()`, `asyncio.gather` and assert no IntegrityError + exactly one coherent row. SQLite round-trips tz-aware datetimes as naive, so compare via a `_naive()` helper.
- Atomic $-budget caps as reservation slots + releasable admission slots (US-190): the per-user/day inference-$ cap AND the global cost breaker are no longer TOCTOU SELECT-sum-vs-threshold reads. They are enforced as finite discrete slots in `human_inference_reservations` (migration 0044): budget is divided into `floor(budget / padrino_human_admission_inference_reserve_usd)` slots; already-charged spend implicitly consumes the lowest slots (`ceil(spent/reserve)`, rounded UP = fail-closed); each admission claims ONE slot atomically via `INSERT ... begin_nested() + IntegrityError-retry` on `uq_human_inference_reservation_slot (scope_key, reservation_day, slot_index)`. `scope_key` is `principal_id.hex` (per-user) or the literal `"GLOBAL"` (breaker) — NO FK, so the global scope needs no sentinel principal row and stays portable across SQLite + Postgres. N concurrent admits can never exceed the slot count, so they cannot overshoot the $ ceiling. `admit_human(...)` claims GLOBAL then per-user inference slots then the count slot; on ANY later short-circuit it DELETEs the reservation rows already claimed in this call (`_rollback_reservations`) so a denial leaks no held budget. KEY slot-allocator invariant for ALL three slot tables (count + both inference): a RELEASED slot frees its CAP budget but KEEPS its physical `slot_index` (a re-claim must pick a FRESH index or it collides on the unique constraint forever). So `_next_free_index(implicit_used, physical)` = lowest int in neither `range(implicit_used)` nor the set of ALL physical indices (released included); the cap is checked separately as `implicit_used + len(live_unreleased) >= cap`. The index may grow above `cap` over a day — fine, the constraint only needs distinctness. `admit_human` returns claimed slot ids on `HumanAdmitDecision {count_slot_id, inference_reservation_ids}`; the lobby route calls `bind_admission_slots(session, decision, lobby_id=, lobby_member_id=)` after creating the lobby/member, and `release_admission_for_lobby` (idle auto-cancel) / `release_admission_for_member` (kick + stale eviction) set `released_at` so an ABANDONED action no longer permanently burns a day-cap slot (caps count actual games/joins, not attempts). An in-request validation failure is already self-healing because `get_session` rolls the whole txn back. Existing equality assertions on an ALLOWED `admit_human` result must switch to `.allowed`/`.reason` (the decision now carries non-default slot ids); DENIED-result equalities still hold (slot ids default None/()).
- Shared human seat authorization (US-170): action/chat/observation/turing shells all consume `api.human_seat_auth.resolve_human_game_seat(...)` for the `GameSeat.occupant_principal_id == principal_id` check and pass their local `wrong_seat` detail through it. Keep future seat-scoped human routes on this helper so auth hardening cannot drift across channels.

- Production-wiring invariant tests (US-169): for human-lane end-to-end gates, drive the real `runner.human_lane._default_human_game_executor(...)` / `_run_one_human_game(...)` path with preseeded `HumanActionSubmission` rows and deterministic AI adapters. Pair AST guards over `runner/human_lane.py` with DB-backed timing/hydration/reveal assertions, then do quick local mutation checks so each acceptance assertion is proven to fail when its production wiring regresses. Avoid ultra-low `0.01s` deadlines in DB-backed human-lane tests on shared in-memory SQLite; cancellation during persistence can corrupt the StaticPool connection, so prefer `>=0.2s` or fake-clock seams.
- Snapshot-backed human request state (US-168): `runner.human_state_cache.resolve_current_human_state(...)` is the request-path resolver for action/chat/observation. The human runtime row now has nullable `state_cache` (migration `0042`) containing a versioned folded `GameState` plus ref-only `StoredEvent` envelopes and `{sequence_head,event_hash_head}`. Request paths trust it only after `game_events[sequence_head].event_hash` matches, then read/fold only `events_repo.list_events_after(..., after_sequence=sequence_head)`; invalid/missing caches fall back to verified full replay. `EventLog.from_stored(...)` reconstructs a trusted cached prefix without rehashing it; suffix rows are still hash-checked as they append. Never put raw human chat in the cache: released human chat remains `text="" + content_ref` in cached envelopes, with raw/cleaned text only in holds/sidecars.
- Crash-consistent paired event persistence (US-189): when a human-lane DB mutation has a paired hash-chain event (seat takeover -> `SeatTakenOver`; chat release -> `content_ref` message), co-commit the `game_events` row in the SAME `session.begin()` as the seat/sidecar/hold write so the DB never gets ahead of the chain (hard rule 4). Use `events_repo.append_event(session, ...)` from the in-memory `StoredEvent` (`stored.sequence`/`prev_event_hash`/`event_hash`). The outer loop's `game_runner._persist_pending_event_rows(persistence, event_log, log_before)` (called by the `persist_pending_events` closure) is idempotent WITHOUT a max-sequence threshold: it reads `events_repo.persisted_sequences_from(session, game_id, from_sequence=log_before)` (the EXACT set of already-committed sequences in the batch) and skips ONLY those. A max-threshold skip is WRONG here: `run_tick` appends `ActionTimedOut` / `OutputInvalid` failure events to the in-memory log at LOWER sequences (persisted nowhere else but this loop), then a chat-release / takeover co-commits its own row at a HIGHER sequence in the SAME tick — so a `sequence <= max_persisted` skip silently drops the lower un-persisted failure rows and a rehydrate from `game_events` reconstructs a divergent state (hard rule 4 violation). Test the invariant two ways: (1) drive only the mutation (skipping the loop) then rehydrate from `game_events` alone (`replay_state_from_rows`) asserting provenance/sequence consistency; (2) build a mixed batch (failure events at seq 0,1 NOT co-committed + a co-committed row pre-persisted at seq 2) and assert `_persist_pending_event_rows` leaves EVERY event_log sequence with a matching `game_events` row and no duplicates.
- Human action rate limiting (US-168, ordering corrected by US-191): `api.human_actions.submit_action(...)` uses dedicated `human-action:*` RateLimitStore buckets and settings `padrino_rate_limit_human_action_per_minute` / `_per_game_phase_per_minute`, separate from the shared human session read bucket and chat buckets. Idempotent action retries are checked before the limiter and remain free. As of US-191 the order is existence/terminal/seat checks -> presence heartbeat -> idempotency -> LEGALITY validation (`legal_actions_for`) -> rate-limit slot consumption -> record. Legality is validated BEFORE a slot is consumed so an illegal / out-of-phase action (incl. the live-game race where a vote target was eliminated between observe and submit) returns 409 WITHOUT burning the seat's budget and can never 429-lock the seat out of its one legal move for the phase. The fixed-window `InMemoryRateLimitStore` has no refund primitive, so the fix is purely reordering (check-then-consume), not a refund-on-reject. Regression test: with `per_minute=1` and `per_game_phase=1`, three self-vote (illegal) tries all 409 and the subsequent legal vote still returns 200.
- Human chat rate-limit fairness (US-167): `api.human_chat.submit_chat(...)` must always enforce rate limits, even when the injected store is `None`; it falls back to a process-local `InMemoryRateLimitStore` rather than allowing unlimited chat. The phase-local bucket is keyed by `(game_id, phase, principal_id)`, not just `(game_id, phase)`, so one seat cannot exhaust another principal's phase budget. Regression tests should use two occupied human seats in the same game/phase with `per_game_phase_limit=1` to prove the second principal's first message still passes.
- Atomic human-chat sidecar sequences (US-166): `human_chat_submissions.next_sidecar_sequence(...)` now reserves from `human_chat_sequence_counters` with dialect-specific `INSERT ... ON CONFLICT DO UPDATE ... RETURNING`, seeding/catching up from existing `HumanChatMessage.sequence` and released hold `sidecar_sequence` rows. Concurrency tests should use a file-backed SQLite engine and multiple async sessions; the shared in-memory StaticPool will not exercise cross-connection uniqueness races. The sidecar `(game_id, sequence)` uniqueness remains intact.
- Atomic human admission slots (US-165): `admit_human(...)` now writes a `HumanCostAdmission` reservation row for every allowed create/join/launch inside the caller's transaction. Caps are modeled as finite `(principal_id, admission_day, bucket, slot_index)` slots protected by `uq_human_cost_admission_slot`; legacy `Game` / `LobbyMember` rows are treated as implicit occupied slots so old data still counts while new route writes are not double-counted. Concurrency tests should use a file-backed SQLite engine, not the shared in-memory fixture, so multiple async sessions can contend for unique slots deterministically. Human-lane spend membership is `{HUMAN, AI_TAKEOVER}`, and daily inference caps filter by `LlmCall.created_at` (charge time), not `Game.created_at`.
- OAuth account upgrade hardening (US-164): the OAuth start route binds the signed `state` payload to `oauth_session_binding(HUMAN_SESSION_COOKIE)` and includes the ID-token nonce in that signed payload; callback must validate both the cookie/query state match and the signed session binding before exchanging code. The default resolver now trusts ONLY a provider `id_token` after Authlib/JWKS validation of signature + `aud == config.client_id` + `iss == config.issuer` + nonce; userinfo is no longer the identity assertion. Tests that need no live provider can either keep using `set_resolve_user_info(...)` for account-linking paths or use `set_exchange_token(...)` + `set_fetch_jwks(...)` with a local signed token to exercise real validation. `_in_flight_guest_id` must mirror `get_human_context`: revoked, expired, deleted, or non-guest sessions are not upgrade candidates.
- Participant-gated endgame reveal (US-163): keep `core.reveal.project_endgame_reveal(...)` as the ONLY reveal schema. The impure shared shell is `api/reveal.py`: it loads `GameSeat` rows, resolves exact model identity via `AgentBuild -> ModelConfig -> ModelProvider`, and can derive terminal winner from either `Game.terminal_result` or a verified replay of `game_events` through `runner.human_durability.replay_state_from_rows`. Public `/public/games/{id}/reveal` still gates on broadcastable `RECENT`; private `/human/games/{id}/reveal` ignores broadcast state but requires a human-session principal occupying a seat, returns 403 for wrong seat, and 409 while the verified game state is not terminal. The dashboard play reveal page should call the human route (`client.humanGameReveal`) for lobby/private games; the public route remains for broadcast/recent spectator games.
- Human disconnect takeover wiring (US-162): human seat liveness lives in `human_seat_presence` rows updated by observation/action/chat routes. The worker lane derives pure `SeatPresence` values from those rows plus the configured reconnect grace, then revalidates an expired HUMAN seat under `SELECT ... FOR UPDATE` immediately before calling `take_over_seat` on the original `SeatMultiplexAdapter`. The appended `SeatTakenOver` event is persisted by `drive_game_loop` through the normal pending-event path before tick responses; `GameSeat` flips to `AI_TAKEOVER`, retains `occupant_principal_id`, and stores `takeover_agent_build_id` / `taken_over_at_phase` for reveal. A reconnect heartbeat before the final recheck cancels takeover; repeated helper calls no-op once `seat_kind` has flipped.
- Human runtime snapshot + resume seam (US-161): the human-lane default executor wires a `phase_snapshot` hook into `drive_game_loop`; the hook writes `HumanGameRuntime` after `PhaseStarted`, after the tick's pending events are persisted, and after `PhaseResolved`. The snapshot stores `phase`, `deadline_at`, and buffer METADATA only: latest structured action per seat plus chat-hold metadata (`ready_for_release`) with NO raw/cleaned chat text duplicated outside the chat hold/sidecar tables. `GameResume` carries the rehydrated `GameState` + `EventLog` + runtime metadata; when the event log already has `PhaseStarted` for the current phase and no `PhaseResolved`, `drive_game_loop` skips re-emitting `PhaseStarted` and appends new events at the existing hash-chain head. `run_human_lane` calls `rehydrate_active_human_games(...)` once at startup and passes the resume state through `GamePersistence`.
- Human-chat content-ref chain seam (US-160): `runner/human_chat_release.release_held_chat_for_phase(..., event_log=event_log)` now does TWO coordinated things at delayed release time: (1) appends a recorded-only core `PublicMessageSubmitted` / `PrivateMessageSubmitted` event to the shared in-memory `EventLog` with `payload.text=""` and `payload.content_ref=human_chat_content_ref(raw_text)`, and (2) writes the sidecar `HumanChatMessage` at the SAME `sequence` with raw+cleaned text. The outer `drive_game_loop` `persist_pending_events(log_before)` then persists the newly appended ref-only event in hash-chain order; do NOT also insert a game_events row inside the release helper on the production path. AI seats in human games see released human text through the impure `runner.human_chat_observation.HumanChatHydratingAdapter`, which loads sidecar `cleaned_text` by sequence and hydrates outbound `Observation` payloads without touching the hash-chained event. The human observation SSE route uses the same hydrator. Tests should assert the persisted event payload contains only `text=""` + `content_ref`, while the sidecar holds raw/cleaned text and the outbound observation has resolved `text`.
- Human-lane production tick seam (US-158): `runner/game_runner.py` now exposes `drive_game_loop(config, adapter, ranked, *, persistence, tick_runner)` while the historical `run_game(...)` wrapper still uses the standard benchmark `run_tick` path. Human-lane code must call `drive_game_loop` with a tick runner that delegates to `runner/human_tick.run_human_tick`, never `run_game`, so the benchmark scheduler/gauntlets stay unchanged and human games get the symmetric release-delay wrapper. Production human seats are assembled by `runner/human_lane.build_human_lane_adapter(session_factory, game_id, settings, ai_adapter_factory=None)`: HUMAN seats get `HumanAdapter(deadline_seconds=settings.padrino_human_phase_deadline_seconds, pull_action=<DB latest_for_phase>)`; AI / AI_TAKEOVER seats keep the curated `GameSeat.agent_build_id`/`takeover_agent_build_id` and are projected through `gauntlets.tournament.project_agent_build` + `gauntlets.heterogeneous.build_heterogeneous_adapter`. Test seam: pass `ai_adapter_factory` to replace only AI providers with deterministic adapters while still exercising production `HumanAdapter` construction. Avoid external POSTs racing a live in-memory SQLite runner append loop; for stable POST-channel assertions, seed a verified phase prefix, POST through the real route, then run one human-aware tick against the replayed state.
- Delayed human-chat release seam (US-159): `api/human_chat.submit_chat(...)` is now validation + rate-limit + moderation + HELD staging only. For ALLOW/SOFT_MASK it stores the moderation-approved `HumanChatSubmission.cleaned_text` and leaves `status='HELD'`; it never creates a `HumanChatMessage` sidecar row, appends a core chat event, or stamps `released_at` in the POST request. The production human-lane tick wrapper calls `runner/human_tick.run_human_tick(...)` first, then invokes `runner/human_chat_release.release_held_chat_for_phase(session, game_id, phase, released_at, event_log=event_log)` after the fixed release delay has elapsed. This release helper moves raw+cleaned text to the sidecar, appends the ref-only recorded chat event (US-160), and flips the hold to RELEASED. Test pattern: assert POST leaves `sidecar == []`, then run `_run_human_tick_responses(..., release_chat=<callback>, clock=_FakeClock.now, sleep=_FakeClock.sleep)` against the US-158 production adapter path and assert the human hold's `released_at` matches the tick's common `settled_at` used for AI messages.
- Mixed human+AI seats + AI takeover via adapter swap (US-139): one game seats a per-seat mix of `HumanAdapter` and LLM adapters wired through the EXISTING `llm/multiplex.py::SeatMultiplexAdapter` (originally US-083 for heterogeneous gauntlets) — the mux IS a single `LlmAdapter`, so `run_game(config, mux, ranked)` drives a mixed game unchanged. US-139 adds `SeatMultiplexAdapter.swap_seat(seat, adapter) -> previous_adapter`: an AI takeover swaps a seat's adapter BETWEEN ticks (rebinds only the dispatch table, raises KeyError on an unknown seat — a takeover replaces an existing occupant, never introduces a seat). The swap holds ZERO game state, so replay is unaffected by when seats were swapped; the takeover itself is recorded as the canonical `SeatTakenOver` event (US-122) committed to the hash-chained log, and `core/engine/reducer.compute_seat_provenance(typed_events)` reconstructs HUMAN_THEN_AI from it (the seat must be `seat_kind="HUMAN"` in `RolesAssigned` for the upgrade; an AI seat stays AI). KEY determinism fact: a game driven with human seats produces a BYTE-IDENTICAL hash chain to the same game driven fully-AI, AS LONG AS each seat emits the same `Action` — drive a `HumanAdapter` from a `pull_action` that returns the seat's scripted action (mirrors the POST channel) so human and AI seats are interchangeable to the engine. NOTE: `game_runner.run_game`'s `RolesAssigned` payload does NOT stamp `seat_kind` (defaults None -> provenance treats as AI); marking seats HUMAN at assignment is the launch-handoff's job (US-149), so the full-game replay tests assert chain/state equality while a SEPARATE small test asserts HUMAN_THEN_AI provenance from a hand-built HUMAN-marked `RolesAssigned`+`SeatTakenOver` log. Test pattern: `tests/runner/test_mixed_seat_replay.py` reuses `tests/conftest.make_town_win_script` + `assign_roles(seed, mini7_v1)`, a `_FakeClock` (advances only on injected sleep), and a `_TakeoverMux` wrapper that fires `mux.swap_seat(...)` once when `observation.phase.startswith("DAY_1_VOTE")` (between ticks). Assert replay via `replay_event_log(log.events)` (hash equality) + `replay_events(typed)` (state equality).
- Human-aware tick + symmetric fixed release delay (US-138): a mixed human+AI game must not let message TIMING out a seat (an LLM answers in seconds; a human takes most of a human-friendly deadline). `runner/human_tick.py::run_human_tick(state, event_log, eligible_seats, adapter, ruleset, config, *, ranked=False, clock=time.monotonic, sleep=asyncio.sleep) -> HumanTickResult` wraps the UNCHANGED `runner/tick.run_tick` (no tick.py contract change): it (1) dispatches ALL seats — `HumanAdapter` and LLM alike — through `run_tick` with `timeout_s=config.phase_deadline_seconds` (the human-friendly per-phase deadline; a slow human is coerced to a safe action by the same hard barrier as a slow LLM, since HumanAdapter resolves its OWN deadline internally and run_tick's asyncio.wait_for is the outer cap), then (2) holds the phase's public messages and releases them after ONE fixed `config.release_delay_seconds` measured on the INJECTED clock — so a human's words and an AI's words surface at the EXACT same instant (`released_at` is identical for every message in the phase; `len({m.released_at}) == 1`). Decision 5 simplified for v1: a FIXED delay, NO seeded jitter / multi-message windows; AI messages wait in the buffer too (inverts the benchmark runner's "emit at tick resolution"). `HumanTickConfig {phase_deadline_seconds, release_delay_seconds}` is plain data fed from settings `padrino_human_phase_deadline_seconds` (120.0) / `padrino_human_release_delay_seconds` (3.0) at the runner seam — the module reads NO settings and NO wall clock itself. Public messages are gated to DAY_DISCUSSION/DAY_VOTE (mirrors `game_runner._submission_events_for`), collected in SEAT order (already-public info) so the released list cannot be used to tell human from AI. `ReleasedMessage {seat_id, text, released_at}`; `HumanTickResult {responses (verbatim run_tick output), released_messages, settled_at}`. The release instant is read AFTER the sleep so it reflects the real viewer-facing clock; the phase always settles within `deadline + release_delay`. ALL delay/clock logic lives in this impure runner module (the purity-firewall test scans ONLY `game_runner.py`, so a sibling runner module may import asyncio/time). DETERMINISTIC test pattern: a `_FakeClock` that advances ONLY when the injected `sleep` is awaited (same shape as US-137's HumanAdapter tests) — inject `clock.now`/`clock.sleep` into BOTH `run_human_tick` AND each `HumanAdapter`, so a never-submitting human polls its deadline (advancing the fake clock) then the fixed release delay is added, all with zero wall-clock. See `tests/runner/test_human_tick_symmetry.py`.
- Live-tail SSE (US-133): the original `/public/games/{id}/live` reads the committed log ONCE via `plan_broadcast` then ends (post-hoc paced replay). True live-tailing of an in-progress game lives in `padrino.public.live_tail.stream_live_tail(session_factory, game_id, *, after, config, on_poll)` — an async generator that (1) emits the committed prefix projected through the EXISTING `public.projection.to_public_event_v1` (identity-blind, drops PRIVATE/SYSTEM, strips FORBIDDEN_PAYLOAD_KEYS) and (2) keeps polling for `sequence > cursor` in a FRESH short-lived `async with session_factory() as session` per poll (NO long-held DB session — required for hours-long human games). The cursor advances past EVERY committed event incl. dropped PRIVATE/SYSTEM ones so resume never re-reads them; only sequences strictly > `after` are emitted so reconnect-by-sequence yields no gaps/dupes. The stream closes on: the committed `GameTerminated` PUBLIC frame (the natural live close), the game reaching terminal (`status==COMPLETED` or `broadcast_state==RECENT`), the game vanishing/non-broadcastable, or `idle_timeout_ms`. Keep-alive = an SSE comment line `": keep-alive\n\n"` emitted after `heartbeat_ms` idle. A LIVE game never exposes `terminal_result` because only projected PUBLIC events are emitted (the column is never read into a frame). Timing is injected via `LiveTailConfig(poll_ms, heartbeat_ms, idle_timeout_ms)` (settings `padrino_sse_live_tail_*`), so tests run instant. The HTTP seam is the existing `/live` endpoint with a new `?tail=true` flag + a `_live_tail_config` FastAPI dependency (override in tests); the one-shot `plan_broadcast` path is untouched when `tail` is false.
- DETERMINISTIC concurrency test for a poll-append loop on the in-memory SQLite engine (StaticPool = ONE shared connection): do NOT race a producer `asyncio.create_task` against the tail — the single shared connection starves the 1ms polls and frames drop intermittently (observed [1,2,4] flake). Instead expose an `on_poll: Callable[[], Awaitable[None]]` hook awaited at the top of each poll iteration and pass a queue of step callbacks; the test grows the log INSIDE the hook (synchronous w.r.t. the loop) so there is no contention. The hook is a legitimate prod seam (no-op when unset), not test-only cruft. See `stream_live_tail(..., on_poll=...)` + `_collect(steps=[...])` in `tests/public/test_live_tail.py`.
- Anonymity guard two-halves (US-124): the EXISTING deny-list (`core/observation_privacy.FORBIDDEN_PAYLOAD_KEYS`) is a PAYLOAD-KEY guard — it only catches forbidden keys nested in an event payload. It does NOT catch a new identity DB COLUMN on a seat/game row that is projected wholesale to a surface. US-124 adds BOTH: (1) `HUMAN_IDENTITY_KEYS` (is_human, controller_type, seat_kind, occupant_principal_id, occupant_user_id, human_player_id, takeover, taken_over_at_phase, takeover_agent_build_id) folded into `FORBIDDEN_PAYLOAD_KEYS` via `frozenset({...}) | HUMAN_IDENTITY_KEYS` — `spectator_projection.SPECTATOR_FORBIDDEN_PAYLOAD_KEYS` is `= FORBIDDEN_PAYLOAD_KEYS` so it inherits them for free (no edit needed there); (2) an ALLOWLIST column guard `project_row_through_allowlist(row, allowlist, *, identity_mode)` + `project_seat_row`/`project_game_row` with `PUBLIC_SEAT_FIELDS`/`PUBLIC_GAME_FIELDS` — anything NOT allowlisted (incl. a future identity column never added to the deny list) is dropped. `assert_anonymous_safe(payload)` raises `AnonymityViolation` on any forbidden key (walks dicts/lists/tuples, inspects KEYS only so it never re-leaks the value).
- FAIL-CLOSED identity mode (US-124): `coerce_identity_mode(mode)` is the SINGLE chokepoint — None / "" / unknown / non-str ALL coerce to ANONYMOUS (strip); ONLY an exact case-insensitive "TRANSPARENT" (also honoring an enum's `.value` attr) opts out. Deliberately kept as bare strings (ANONYMOUS/TRANSPARENT consts) in `observation_privacy.py` so the pure guard has NO forward dependency on the `IdentityMode` enum that US-126 introduces. `project_row_through_allowlist` runs `assert_anonymous_safe` on the projected dict whenever the (coerced) mode is anonymous, so a forbidden key mistakenly added to an allowlist still fails closed.
- Scheduler/async DB tests on the in-memory SQLite engine (`sqlite+aiosqlite:///:memory:`, StaticPool = ONE shared connection) are sensitive to poll ORDER. A status-watcher coroutine that polls `gauntlets_repo.get` in a tight loop must `await asyncio.sleep(interval)` FIRST and read AFTER — reading first then sleeping starves the scheduler's drive/write coroutines of the single shared connection and the gauntlet never finalizes (the run hangs).
