Keep the cooperative `for _ in range(N): await sleep; read; if done: break` shape; raise N for a generous deterministic budget instead of converting to an unbounded `while True` (unbounded + read-first = deadlock under the StaticPool). Never `stop.set()` unconditionally before the target status is observed — that cuts a slow-but-correct run short and makes the final status assertion flaky. See `_drive_scheduler_until` in `tests/runner/test_scheduler.py`.
- Hermetic Playwright e2e for a public-surface page: intercept every `/public/*` call the page makes with `page.route('**/public/<path>*', ...)`, gating on `route.request().resourceType()` in `('fetch','xhr')` and `route.continue()` otherwise (so document/asset loads pass through). This is the lobby/recap/watch pattern; `games.spec.ts` and `leaderboard.spec.ts` now follow it so they no longer depend on whatever the smoke harness happens to seed into the broadcast/ingest indexes (which post-US-112 excludes unverified ingests, making row presence state-dependent). The replay scrub path needs `/public/games/{id}/events*` mocked with >=2 distinct `phase` values and a terminal `GameTerminated` frame so the phase pills + next/prev disabled states are deterministic.
- Per-test Postgres isolation for migration cycle tests: a session-scoped container shared across tests must NOT share one mutable database (leftover objects break the next `upgrade head`). Create a UNIQUE throwaway database per test (`CREATE DATABASE padrino_mig_<uuid>` on an AUTOCOMMIT connection to the maintenance DB — CREATE/DROP DATABASE cannot run in a transaction), point `PADRINO_DB_URL` at it, and `DROP DATABASE` (after `pg_terminate_backend` of lingering sessions) in teardown. Swap the URL path with `urlsplit`/`urlunsplit`. See `_with_database` + the `postgres_db_url` fixture in `tests/db/test_migrations_all_dialects.py`.
- CLI logging is configured ONCE in the Typer `@app.callback()` (`_configure_logging_callback` in `cli.py`), which runs for every subcommand. To honor an env-driven setting across serve/scheduler/bootstrap, read it there from `get_settings().padrino_log_level` rather than per-command. `configure_logging` is idempotent (`_configured` flag), so the callback firing on every invocation is safe. Test the callback by patching `padrino.logging.configure_logging` to capture the level, stub the command body (`uvicorn.run`, `asyncio.run`, `create_engine`), set `PADRINO_LOG_LEVEL`, and call `get_settings.cache_clear()` before invoking via `typer.testing.CliRunner`.
- Pure-planner + impure-executor split: a pure function under `core/` or `db/retention.py` returns a plan (list of ids); the impure executor (`db/retention_executor.py`) loads the projection, calls the planner with an injected `now`, and applies the plan inside `async with session_factory() as session, session.begin()`. Guard destructive jobs with TWO settings — an enable flag AND a `*_dry_run: bool = True` default — both must flip before any row is mutated.
- Deleting a `games` row in tests/executors: child FKs (`game_seats`, `game_events`, `llm_calls`, `rating_events`) DO NOT have `ondelete="CASCADE"` (only `behavioral_evaluations` does), and the SQLite test engine runs with `PRAGMA foreign_keys = ON`, so a bare `DELETE FROM games` raises `FOREIGN KEY constraint failed`. Delete children explicitly (children-first) — this also makes the job portable to Postgres.
- To get an affected-row count from a bulk `UPDATE`/`DELETE` without mypy `Result has no attribute rowcount` errors: run a `select(func.count())` with the SAME where-clause first, then issue the mutation. Cleaner than casting `CursorResult` and keeps the count idempotent (re-runs naturally count zero once the predicate no longer matches).
- Seeding a `GameSeat`/`Rating`/`RatingEvent` in a DB test requires the FK parent chain (`ModelProvider -> ModelConfig + PromptVersion -> AgentBuild`, and `League`) because FKs are enforced under SQLite PRAGMA. Use a `_seed_parents(session) -> (build_id, league_id)` helper rather than `uuid.uuid4()` placeholders.
- Driving a REAL game end-to-end in a test (no real LLM): reuse `_seed_roster` from `tests/scheduler/test_continuous_matchmaking.py` (active League + 7 active AgentBuilds via the prompt/provider/model_config/build repo chain), then call `run_continuous_matchmaking_tick(session_factory, settings=Settings(padrino_enable_continuous_matchmaking=True), now=..., guard=..., adapter_factory=lambda _builds: <MockAdapter>())`. The tick runs ONE game to the MAX_DAYS draw, writes analytics aggregates (`AnalyticsAggregate` rows), runs the moderation gate, and promotes the game to `broadcast_state=LIVE` / `is_broadcastable=True` in one call.
- To make a mock adapter emit `PublicMessageSubmitted` events (so the moderation gate has real chat to inspect): subclass the NoopMockAdapter pattern but on `PhaseKind.DAY_DISCUSSION` set `public_message` on the coerced `AgentResponse` (`base.model_copy(update={"public_message": ...})`). The runner only emits `PublicMessageSubmitted` when `response.public_message` is set AND the phase is DAY_DISCUSSION/DAY_VOTE (`runner/game_runner.py:402`). Use `padrino.llm.mock._phase_kind_for(observation.phase)` to map the phase id to a `PhaseKind`.
- The terminal frame of a game's public SSE stream is `GameTerminated` (visibility=PUBLIC, last event by sequence). To assert an SSE stream is complete + ordered: parse `id:`/`data:` blocks, assert `seqs == sorted(seqs)`, every frame's keys == `PUBLIC_EVENT_V1_FIELDS` with `schema_version == "public_event_v1"` and `visibility == "PUBLIC"`, and `frames[-1]["data"]["event_type"] == "GameTerminated"`.
- Recap analytics (`/public/games/{id}/analytics` for RECENT) legitimately expose aggregate `role` keys (role_win_rates, survival_curve by role) and `claimed_role` on self-claims — these are NOT spoilers because they carry no player_id->hidden-role linkage. Do NOT run the per-event `FORBIDDEN_PAYLOAD_KEYS` walker over the recap body; that deny-list is for live broadcast event PAYLOADS only. Assert recap spoiler-safety structurally (claim records expose only `player_id`/`claimed_role`/`sequence`/`phase`).
- Materialize-at-promotion pattern: a finished game's per-game recap analytics are immutable (the event log is frozen post-terminal), so compute them ONCE at the RECENT transition and persist, instead of re-deriving the full event log per request. `src/padrino/public/game_analytics_store.py` splits a PURE `build_game_analytics_payload(events) -> dict` (the JSON-able full/outcome-revealing shape, shared by the materializer AND the route's LIVE on-the-fly path) from the impure `materialize_game_analytics(session, game_id, *, ruleset_id)` (loads events, builds payload, upserts `MaterializedGameAnalytics` keyed by `game_id`) + `get_materialized_analytics`. `mark_recent` (in `public/broadcast_index.py`) calls the materializer (lazy import to keep the seam local). The GET route serves the stored row for RECENT and SELF-HEALS a stored-missing RECENT game (promoted pre-US-120) by computing + persisting on the fly; LIVE games keep the spoiler-safe on-the-fly path and never read/write the row (the stored blob carries the winner). New table = ONE new Alembic revision (0022), `game_id` PK with `ondelete=CASCADE` to `games.id`. mypy gotcha: a variable assigned `dict` in one branch then `dict | None` in another narrows function-wide — use a distinct variable name for the nullable-then-coalesced path rather than reassigning the same name.
- Making an existing NOT-NULL FK column nullable (Wave 9 made `GameSeat.agent_build_id` nullable for human seats): SQLite cannot ALTER a column's nullability in place, so the migration MUST use `with op.batch_alter_table("game_seats") as batch_op: batch_op.alter_column("agent_build_id", existing_type=sa.Uuid(), nullable=True)` (batch = table rebuild on SQLite, native ALTER on Postgres). Add new columns + `create_foreign_key(name, ...)` inside the SAME batch; downgrade reverses in LIFO order (drop_constraint by name -> drop_column -> alter_column back to nullable=False). A NOT-NULL-with-`server_default` column (`seat_kind server_default "AI"`) keeps every existing row byte-identical after upgrade. Relaxing a NOT-NULL FK to nullable surfaces mypy errors at EVERY consumer of that attribute (`completion.py`, `leaderboards/service.py`, `export/bundle.py`, and tests): guard each with `if seat.agent_build_id is None: continue` (or `assert ... is not None` in AI-only gauntlet paths) — this is the correct fix, never `# type: ignore`.
- Adding an OPTIONAL pure-data field to a frozen core state model (`Seat.seat_kind: SeatKind | None = None`): default it to None so replaying any pre-existing event log reproduces identical state (the reducer's `Seat(...)` construction in `RolesAssigned` does not set it, so it stays None) and mechanics are provably unaffected. Test by folding a legacy `[GameCreated, RolesAssigned, PhaseStarted]` log and asserting every `seat.seat_kind is None` plus byte-stable re-replay.
- Adding a new core event to the discriminated union touches SEVEN spots in `core/engine/events.py` (Payload class, Event class, the `Event = Annotated[... | NewEvent]` union member, `EventAdapter` is auto-derived from `Event`, `EVENT_TYPES` tuple, `__all__` x2) — plus, for a provenance-only/recorded-only event, add it to `reducer._RECORDED_ONLY` so `apply_event` returns state unchanged (NOT a new `isinstance` branch). The existing `tests/core/test_events.py` has TWO catalog-coverage tests (`test_event_types_catalog_covers_all_classes`, `test_every_event_class_has_a_round_trip_sample`) that BOTH fail unless you add a representative instance to `_all_events()` AND the literal set — update them in the same change.
- Deriving per-seat provenance from the event log (US-122 `compute_seat_provenance(event_log) -> {pid: 'HUMAN'|'AI'|'HUMAN_THEN_AI'}`): seed each pid from its `RolesAssigned` `SeatAssignment.seat_kind` (HUMAN -> 'HUMAN', everything incl. None -> 'AI' so legacy AI-only logs are all 'AI'), then every `SeatTakenOver` upgrades a 'HUMAN' seat to 'HUMAN_THEN_AI' (an already-AI seat stays 'AI'). `SeatAssignment` gained an OPTIONAL `seat_kind: SeatKind | None = None` so the provenance source lives IN the hashed event (the reducer wires it onto `Seat.seat_kind`); default None keeps existing RolesAssigned events replay-identical. SeatTakenOver is SYSTEM-visibility, payload carries ONLY pure data (public_player_id, day, phase, reason, replacement_agent_build_ref) — no wall-clock/random. mypy: a mixed-event test list must be annotated `list[Event]` (list invariance rejects `list[RolesAssigned]` at a `list[Event]` param even for a single-type list).
- Segregation: dormant sibling human-rating + zero-write proof (US-125). The scientific Rating/RatingEvent write path has a SINGLE chokepoint — `_should_apply_ratings(persistence, ranked, state)` in `runner/game_runner.py` — which already fails closed for the human lane on TWO independent grounds: (1) `ranked=False` (the human lane is always casual) and (2) `all(seat.public_player_id in persistence.agent_builds ...)` is False whenever a HUMAN seat (no agent build) is present. So a human-lane game writes ZERO scientific rows by construction; no code change to the rating service was needed. The sibling `human_rating` / `human_rating_event` tables (keyed by `human_player_id` instead of `agent_build_id`, mirroring the Rating/RatingEvent column shape) are created DORMANT and never written in v1 — they exist so future activation is a flag-flip not a migration. League gained a `kind` discriminator (`LeagueKind {SCIENTIFIC (default), HUMANS_INCLUDED}` in `core/enums.py`; column server_default 'SCIENTIFIC' so every existing league row is byte-identical) so scientific vs human leagues are queryable; `leagues_repo.get_or_create_humans_included(session, ruleset_id=...)` is the idempotent get-or-create for the single ranked=False / kind=HUMANS_INCLUDED row. Migration 0025 chains off 0024 (current head): `batch_alter_table("leagues").add_column(kind)` + `create_table` x2; downgrade drops the two tables then the column. The segregation test drives a REAL game to terminal (reusing the `tests/runner/test_rating_integration.py` seed pattern + `make_town_win_script` + `DeterministicMockAdapter`) with some seats human-occupied (omitted from `agent_builds`) and asserts `func.count()` over Rating/RatingEvent/HumanRating/HumanRatingEvent is all 0 — for BOTH the casual `ranked=False` path AND a defensive `ranked=True` path (proving the human-seat guard fails closed even if ranked were mis-set). The scientific Rating/RatingEvent tables + their byte-shape are UNTOUCHED.
- Canonical composition counts + IdentityMode (US-126): composition disclosure must be "counts only, never the seat map" across FOUR surfaces (lobby/live/spectator/observation). The SINGLE producer is `core/composition.py::composition_summary(seats) -> CompositionSummary {human_count, ai_count, total}` (pure, data-in, no IO). It is deliberately polymorphic on the seat shape (`_seat_kind_of` accepts a core `Seat`, DB `GameSeat`, a `Mapping` with a `seat_kind` key, a raw `SeatKind`, or a bare string) so every surface can feed it whatever it has. Counts are FROZEN at game start: `SeatKind.AI_TAKEOVER` counts as HUMAN (the seat STARTED human), so a silent takeover (HUMAN -> AI_TAKEOVER) leaves counts unchanged (this is the US-142 guarantee, proven now). Unknown/missing kind fails closed to AI (never inflates the human count). `IdentityMode {ANONYMOUS (default), TRANSPARENT}` lives in `core/enums.py`; the fail-closed COERCION chokepoint stays string-based in `observation_privacy.coerce_identity_mode` (no dependency on the enum) — the enum is just the typed surface. `games.identity_mode` column is NOT NULL server_default 'ANONYMOUS' (every pre-Wave-9 game byte-identical, frozen after start). Migration 0026 chains off the CURRENT head 0025 (NOT 0024 as the AC literally says — US-123 is 0024 but the linear chain advanced; keep it linear off head). `batch_alter_table("games").add_column(identity_mode)`; downgrade drops it. The `session_factory` fixture replays migrations to head, so DB tests exercise the new column automatically.
- Out-of-band human-chat sidecar (US-123, the GDPR-vs-hash-chain fix): raw human chat (PII) must be redactable WITHOUT changing any `event_hash`, which is impossible if it lives inside a hashed event. Solution = a `content_ref` indirection. Add an OPTIONAL `content_ref: str | None = None` to BOTH `PublicMessageSubmittedPayload` and `PrivateMessageSubmittedPayload` (default None keeps every existing/AI event byte-identical — AI text stays inline as before). For a HUMAN seat the paired event payload sets `text=""` and `content_ref=human_chat_content_ref(raw)` (pure `sha256:<hex>` over the utf-8 text, in `src/padrino/core/human_chat.py`); the raw/cleaned text lives ONLY in the new `human_chat_messages` sidecar table keyed by (game_id, sequence). Because the hashed payload carries only the deterministic ref, `human_chat.redact(game_id, sequence)` (nulls raw_text/cleaned_text + sets redacted=True via an UPDATE that touches ONLY the sidecar) leaves every `game_events` row byte-identical, so `verify_chain` still passes post-redaction. To assert this in a DB test: seal bodies through an in-memory `EventLog` to get correct prev/event hashes, persist via `events_repo.append_event`, snapshot `[(seq, event_hash)]` before redaction, redact, then assert the snapshot is unchanged AND `verify_chain(EventEnvelope-from-rows) == head_before`. `content_ref` is pure data (a hash, not wall-clock/random) so it is safe inside the hashed event and the chat-firewall holds (the ref drives no mechanics). New-table migration = ONE Alembic revision chaining off the current head; the `session_factory` test fixture uses `Base.metadata.create_all`, so adding the ORM class is enough for the table to exist in tests (no migration replay needed there).
- Browser-human auth, separate from API-key auth (US-127): the human identity layer is a parallel, provably non-overlapping path to `api/auth.py`. `api/human_auth.py::get_human_context` reads ONLY the `padrino_human_session` cookie (never the Authorization header / api_keys), returns `HumanPrincipalContext | None` (optional resolver, never raises); `require_human()` -> 401 if None; `require_account()` -> 403 for a guest (depends on require_human so a missing session is still 401, not 403). The two directions of non-overlap are TESTABLE without new product routes: in the test, `create_app(auth_required=True)` then `app.include_router` a tiny router with `Depends(require_human)`, `Depends(require_account)`, and `Depends(require_read)` (the existing api-key dep) endpoints — a guest cookie on the api-key route is 401, an api-key Bearer on the human route is 401. Token minting (`secrets.token_urlsafe`) lives in the IMPURE shell `human_auth.generate_session_token` (mirroring `auth.generate_raw_key`), NOT in the repository — `tests/db/test_repositories.py::test_repository_modules_have_no_forbidden_imports` forbids `{random, secrets, time, litellm, httpx}` in `db/repositories/*.py`, so a repo may only `hashlib`-hash the token, never generate it. Per-principal rate limiting REUSES the app's injected `RateLimiter` via the private `auth._get_rate_limiter`/`_get_auth_settings` helpers, keyed `f"human:{session_hash}"` so it shares no bucket with any api_key; setting `padrino_rate_limit_human_per_minute` (default 120). SQLite drops tzinfo on a stored `DateTime(timezone=True)`, so `get_human_context` coerces a naive `expires_at` back to UTC-aware before the `<= now` expiry comparison (`_as_aware`) — otherwise comparing naive vs aware raises TypeError.
- Guest quickplay route + session-cookie minting (US-128): the FIRST endpoint that SETS a `padrino_human_session` cookie (US-127 only read it). `api/routes/human.py::POST /human/guest` mints `generate_session_token()` (the impure shell), `create_principal(kind=guest)` + `create_session(...)` (token stored only as sha256 via the repo), then `response.set_cookie(key=HUMAN_SESSION_COOKIE, value=raw_token, httponly=True, secure=settings.padrino_human_session_cookie_secure, samesite="lax", path="/", max_age=ttl_hours*3600)`. The router is mounted UNCONDITIONALLY in `app.py` (alongside health/public, NOT inside the `if not surface_only:` block and with NO API-scope `Depends`), so it is reachable under `create_app(auth_required=True)` AND the public-surface-only deployment — humans play from the public site. Two new settings: `padrino_human_session_ttl_hours: int = 720`, `padrino_human_session_cookie_secure: bool = True` (flip off via `PADRINO_HUMAN_SESSION_COOKIE_SECURE=false` + `get_settings.cache_clear()` for a plain-http test client; the ASGI test transport over http:// still RECEIVES a Secure-flagged Set-Cookie header so cookie ATTRIBUTE assertions work regardless, but a Secure cookie won't be RESENT by httpx on http:// — pass the token explicitly via `cookies={HUMAN_SESSION_COOKIE: token}` in follow-up requests). `PATCH /human/me` (display name, `Field(min_length=1, max_length=40)` + a strip-non-blank `field_validator` so "   " is 422, NOT globally unique) and `GET /human/me` both `Depends(require_human)` (401 without a session). To parse + assert Set-Cookie attributes in a test: iterate `resp.headers.get_list("set-cookie")`, load the matching one into `http.cookies.SimpleCookie`, then check `morsel["httponly"]`, `morsel["samesite"].lower()=="lax"`, `morsel["path"]=="/"`; when Secure is OFF the morsel's `secure` is the empty string `""`.
- Durable, rehydratable human-game state (US-131): the human runner is in-memory; a minutes-to-hours human game must survive a process restart. Pattern = a one-row-per-game `human_game_runtime` table (PK game_id, FK ondelete=CASCADE) holding ONLY impure live scaffolding — `phase`, `deadline_at` (nullable), `buffer_snapshot` (JSON of in-flight per-seat human submissions), `updated_at`. The deterministic core `GameState` is NEVER stored there: `runner/human_durability.py::rehydrate_active_human_games(session_factory)` reconstructs it by REPLAYING the hash-chained `game_events` log (hard rule 4 — if the snapshot ever disagreed, the event log wins). The replay path REUSES the export/bundle `_event_body` shape (`event_type, sequence, phase, visibility, actor_player_id, payload` — sequence IS in the hashed body; event_hash/prev_event_hash/created_at are excluded by hashing.py) to rebuild `StoredEvent`s, runs them through the PURE `replay_event_log` (which re-seals + raises ReplayHashMismatchError on any tampered hash), then folds the same bodies through `apply_event` to get the state. Eligibility: a runtime row's game must be NOT terminal (status != "COMPLETED" AND replayed `state.terminal_result is None` — a stale row for a game that finished pre-restart is skipped, never resumed) AND human-lane (at least one GameSeat with seat_kind in {HUMAN, AI_TAKEOVER}; AI-only benchmark games are untouched). Returns a frozen `RehydratedHumanGame {game_id, state, event_log, phase, deadline_at, buffer_snapshot}` list sorted by game_id for determinism. SQLite-tz gotcha (same as US-127): `DateTime(timezone=True)` loads back tz-NAIVE on SQLite, so `_as_aware()` coerces `deadline_at` back to UTC-aware on rehydrate (else the resumed deadline != the persisted one). The repo `db/repositories/human_game_runtime.py` (upsert/get/list_all/delete) imports only `datetime` for typing — NO `time`/`secrets`/`random` (repo-purity guard); `deadline_at`/`updated_at` are passed in from the impure shell. `human_durability.py` is a NEW runner module (the `test_game_runner_does_not_import_forbidden_modules` purity guard scans ONLY `game_runner.py`, so this module may import `datetime`). Migration 0030 chains off head 0029 (AC says "after US-130"/0029 — matches). DB-test seats leave `agent_build_id=None` for ALL seats (nullable since US-121) to avoid seeding a real agent-build FK chain just to set seat_kind; rehydration only reads seat_kind. New tables/migrations need no extra migration-test wiring — `tests/db/test_migrations*.py` replay to head and exercise 0030's up/down round-trip automatically.
- One-tap consent + 16+ age gate (US-130): a human must accept TOS + PRIVACY + AGE_GATE before sending any action or chat, captured with one tap. Pattern = APPEND-ONLY `human_consents` table (NEVER updated in place; a re-accept appends fresh rows) + a settings-driven version check so a bump RE-PROMPTS. The "current version" of each document lives in `Settings` (`padrino_consent_tos_version` / `_privacy_version` / `_age_gate_version`, all default "2026-06-18"). A consent is "current" for a kind only when its stored `document_version` EQUALS the settings value — so bumping any one version silently drops that kind from `current_consent_kinds` until the human re-accepts (`has_current_consent` = `kinds >= REQUIRED_DOCUMENT_KINDS`). Enforcement is in the api/runner shell ONLY (NEVER core): `api/human_consent.py::enforce_consent(session, *, subject_principal_id, settings)` raises `HTTPException(412, detail="consent_required")` when the principal lacks a complete current consent — the US-134/135 action/chat channels call this before accepting input. `record_consent` writes one row per `REQUIRED_DOCUMENT_KINDS` member at the current versions and hashes the client IP (`hash_source_ip` -> sha256, never the raw IP; `client_ip_hash(request)` reads `request.client.host`). Routes added to the existing `api/routes/human.py` router (already mounted unconditionally): `POST /human/consent` (one-tap, `require_human`, 201) + `GET /human/consent` (status: `{consented, required_versions}`). To TEST a consent gate before the real action channel exists, mount a tiny `_test/human/act` router whose endpoint `Depends(require_human)` then calls `enforce_consent` — exactly how the real channel will gate; bump a version via `monkeypatch.setenv(... )` + `get_settings.cache_clear()` + a fresh `create_app` to prove re-prompt. Repo (`db/repositories/human_consents.py`) has NO secrets/time import (repo-purity guard) — the IP hash + version resolution live in the API shell. Migration 0029 chains off head 0028 (the AC says "after US-127"/0027 but the chain advanced; keep it linear off head).
- Separate human-game worker lane (US-132): minutes-to-hours human games must not pin the benchmark scheduler's tiny concurrency cap (`padrino_max_concurrent_games`=3, sized for ~45s model turns). The fix is a SEPARATE worker pool, not just separate accounting. `runner/human_lane.py::run_human_lane(session_factory, *, concurrency, stop_event, ...)` is a dedicated drain loop with its OWN `asyncio.Semaphore(concurrency)` (default `padrino_human_lane_max_concurrent`=5) and its own claim path — it shares NO semaphore, queue, or claim path with `runner/scheduler.py::run_scheduler`. Lane membership is a property of the GAME not the loop: a game is "human-lane" iff a `GameSeat` has `seat_kind in {HUMAN, AI_TAKEOVER}` (`_HUMAN_LANE_SEAT_KINDS`). Isolation is structural, not just by-cap: the benchmark scheduler claims via `gauntlets_repo.claim_oldest_pending` (keys off Gauntlet rows) and human games are gauntlet-less (`gauntlet_id=None`), so the benchmark lane can NEVER pick up a human game and vice-versa (the human lane filters on seat_kind). `list_human_lane_games(session, statuses=...)` returns human-lane game ids in a status set (default `{CREATED, PENDING, RUNNING}` — RUNNING is claimable so a post-restart resume re-drives an in-flight game; `_claim_game` is idempotent: it returns the game WITHOUT re-flipping when already RUNNING, and returns None for a COMPLETED/vanished/non-human game so no double-run). The in-process `tasks: dict[game_id, Task]` dedupes dispatch within one loop; `run_game` itself skips-if-COMPLETED (game_runner.py:293) so a re-listed RUNNING game is a no-op once finished. `human_lane_admission(session_factory, *, capacity) -> HumanLaneAdmission{in_flight, waiting, capacity, available}` is the lane's OWN admission snapshot (counts RUNNING vs CREATED/PENDING human-lane games) — it never reads the benchmark queue. CLI: `padrino human-lane [--concurrency N] [--db-url ...]` is a SEPARATE process from `padrino scheduler` (mirrors the scheduler command's signal-handler + engine-dispose shape; resolves concurrency from `padrino_human_lane_max_concurrent` when the flag is omitted). The finally-block drains in-flight tasks via `asyncio.gather(..., return_exceptions=True)` so no orphan task leaks a DB session. Human-lane games run casual (`run_game(..., ranked=False)`) with `agent_builds={}` so the rating write path fails closed (segregation, hard rule 8). `human_lane.py` is a NEW runner module — the purity-firewall test scans ONLY `game_runner.py`, so sibling runner modules may import asyncio/db/wall-clock. Test isolation proof (`tests/runner/test_human_lane_isolation.py`): a saturated human lane (cap 1, many waiting) lets an INDEPENDENT benchmark `Semaphore(3)` acquire all 3 slots while the human lane stays pinned to its single slot — concurrency is provably not stolen. Test seam: `game_executor` is injected (a barrier/counting executor) so the suite never runs real mini7 games; `_drain_until(predicate, timeout_s)` cooperatively polls with a deterministic budget (NOT an unbounded while-True).
- Authenticated human chat channel into the buffered hold (US-135): a human submits a public/private chat message over `POST /human/games/{game_id}/chat` (on the existing unconditionally-mounted human router). UNLIKE the action channel, chat NEVER mutates state — it parks in a buffer HOLD and is released only after the block-before-release moderation hook (US-140) passes. Pattern = a `human_chat_submissions` hold table (`db/models.py`): id PK, game_id FK (ondelete=CASCADE), public_player_id, phase, channel, idempotency_key, raw_text, `status` ('HELD'|'RELEASED'|'BLOCKED', server_default 'HELD'), nullable `sidecar_sequence`, created_at, nullable released_at; UNIQUE `(game_id, public_player_id, phase, idempotency_key)` for idempotent retries. The hold raw_text is transient staging; on RELEASE the raw + cleaned text is routed to the US-123 `human_chat_messages` SIDECAR (`human_chat.append_human_chat`) so it is GDPR-redactable and NEVER inline in a hash-chained payload (the eventual paired core event carries only a content_ref — that chaining is US-138/140's job, NOT US-135). The impure service `api/human_chat.py::submit_chat(session, *, game_id, principal_id, channel, text, idempotency_key, now, moderation=None)` (1) resolves the seat via `occupant_principal_id` (403 wrong_seat); (2) rejects empty (422) / over-limit-per-channel (422, double-checking the schema's `max_length=600` against `ruleset.PUBLIC/PRIVATE_MESSAGE_MAX_CHARS`); (3) replays the chain via `replay_state_from_rows` and validates the CHANNEL is legal for the phase (PUBLIC in DAY_DISCUSSION/DAY_VOTE; PRIVATE only a MAFIA seat in NIGHT_0_MAFIA_INTRO/NIGHT_MAFIA_DISCUSSION; terminal/dead -> 409 chat_not_allowed); (4) idempotency short-circuit; (5) records HELD, runs the moderation hook, then on ALLOW/SOFT_MASK writes the sidecar at `next_sidecar_sequence(game_id)` (a per-game monotonic ordinal over existing sidecar_sequence rows — a placeholder until US-140 chains a real game_events sequence) and flips to RELEASED; on BLOCK flips to BLOCKED and never releases. The MODERATION SEAM is `api/human_chat_moderation.py`: an async `ChatModerationHook` Protocol + `ChatModerationVerdict {verdict: ChatVerdict(ALLOW/SOFT_MASK/BLOCK), cleaned_text}` + a v1 `StubPassModerationHook` (ALLOW unchanged) — US-140 swaps the real deterministic-first-pass + guard-model verdict in WITHOUT touching the channel (hook is async so the guard call drops in). The request model `ChatSubmission {channel: Literal['PUBLIC','PRIVATE'], text, idempotency_key}` uses `extra='forbid'` so a stray structured `action` field is a 422 (chat firewall — the inverse of US-134's stray-`public_message` 422). Route gates on `enforce_consent` (US-130) before accepting. Repo `db/repositories/human_chat_submissions.py` imports only `datetime` for typing (repo-purity guard; created_at/released_at injected from the shell). Migration 0032 chains off head 0031. Test seeds a non-terminal game at DAY_1_DISCUSSION (PhaseStarted phase_kind DAY_DISCUSSION) so PUBLIC chat is legal, links the human seat via `occupant_principal_id`, and asserts held-then-released routes raw text to the sidecar / over-limit 422 / idempotent retry inserts no second hold or sidecar row / stray action 422 / 401 / 412.
- Per-seat live observation stream + phase-deadline frame (US-136): a human's client gets an authenticated, seat-scoped live stream of ITS OWN observation (private_events, legal_actions, you.role/faction) plus a transport-only phase-deadline frame. Route `GET /human/games/{game_id}/observation/stream` on the existing unconditionally-mounted human router, `Depends(require_human)` (401 without a session). The impure shell `api/human_observation.py::build_seat_observation_snapshot(session, *, game_id, principal_id)` (1) resolves the caller's seat via `GameSeat.occupant_principal_id` (no seat -> 403 `wrong_seat`); (2) replays the chain via `runner.human_durability.replay_state_from_rows` (the SHARED verified-replay path) to get `(state, event_log)`; (3) resolves `get_ruleset(game.ruleset_id)` and REUSES the PURE `core.observations.build_observation(state, core_seat, event_log, ruleset)` — NO new branching in core (US-141 adds the mode-aware build_observation variant; US-136 just consumes the existing identity-blind one); (4) reads the wall-clock deadline from the `human_game_runtime` row (US-131) — the deadline is TRANSPORT-ONLY, never written to a hashed event (hard rule 4). KEY PATTERN: the snapshot (incl. seat resolution + replay) is built in the ROUTE BODY *before* returning `StreamingResponse(stream_snapshot(snapshot), media_type="text/event-stream")`, so a wrong-seat/not-found error surfaces as a real 403/404 HTTP status rather than a half-open SSE stream that already sent a 200 header (an HTTPException raised INSIDE the generator cannot set the status code — the body has begun). Frames are `data: {json}\n\n` blocks each carrying a `type` discriminator (`observation`/`phase_deadline`). ANONYMITY: build_observation is identity-blind by construction (carries no human/AI/model markers), but the seat legitimately sees its OWN `you.role`/`you.faction` (hard rule 3), so the broad `assert_anonymous_safe` (which forbids role/faction) is TOO aggressive here — added a NARROWER `core/observation_privacy.assert_no_identity_markers(payload)` keyed on the new `IDENTITY_MARKER_KEYS = HUMAN_IDENTITY_KEYS | MODEL_IDENTITY_KEYS` (model markers = agent_build_id/model_id/model_name/provider/provider_name/gauntlet_clone_index/clone_index) that walks dicts/lists and raises only on an identity marker, never on the seat's allowed self-role. The shell runs it over the observation frame whenever `is_anonymous(game.identity_mode)` (fail closed). SQLite-tz gotcha (same as US-127/131): `DateTime(timezone=True)` loads back tz-NAIVE on SQLite, so a local `_as_aware()` coerces the deadline back to UTC-aware before `.isoformat()` (else the emitted deadline string drops the `+00:00` and != the persisted one). No migration (no schema change); pure-core firewall untouched (build_observation unchanged; the new guard is pure-data key-walking). Test seeds a non-terminal game at DAY_1_VOTE + a `human_game_runtime` row with a deadline, links the human seat via `occupant_principal_id`, and asserts: the seat sees its own `you.player_id` + `legal_actions`; no event payload carries another seat's role/faction; the deadline frame matches the seeded `_DEADLINE.isoformat()`; no `IDENTITY_MARKER_KEYS` appear in any frame in anonymous mode; wrong-seat -> 403; no session -> 401.
- Composition-counts disclosure surfaces (US-142): every player/spectator/lobby surface that shows composition discloses ONLY counts ("N humans, M AI"), never a per-seat map, and the counts are FROZEN at game start (a silent AI takeover does NOT change them). The single translation seam between the canonical pure counter (`core/composition.composition_summary`, US-126) and the API response is `public/composition_disclosure.py::composition_counts(seats) -> CompositionCounts {human_count, ai_count, total}` (a Pydantic model carrying ONLY counts — there is NO per-seat field, so a surface returning this model structurally cannot leak a human/AI seat map). Surfaces feed it their seat rows (DB `GameSeat` or core `Seat` — `composition_summary` is polymorphic on seat shape); they NEVER count seats themselves. The takeover-frozen guarantee is inherited free from `composition_summary` (`SeatKind.AI_TAKEOVER` counts as HUMAN because the seat STARTED human). - Invite links, roster, ready-up, presence (US-148): a host shares an invite link; friends (guest or signed-in) join, ready up, and the host can lock/kick/transfer; idle/abandoned lobbies auto-cancel. Schema delta = ONE unique `Lobby.invite_token` column (NOT NULL); migration 0036 adds it nullable, backfills `secrets.token_urlsafe(24)` per existing row, then enforces NOT NULL + UNIQUE inside `batch_alter_table` (SQLite needs the rebuild for the constraint; `secrets` is legal in a migration, NOT in a repo). The invite token is a SHAREABLE address, not a one-time code: single-use-per-person is enforced by the `uq_lobby_member(lobby_id, principal_id)` unique constraint — re-joining is idempotent (returns the existing membership, never a second row). `POST /lobbies/join/{invite_token}` adds a `LobbyMember` ONLY (no seat mutation — seat materialization/auto-fill is US-149's launch-handoff job), so composition stays counts-only and frozen at the host's create-time config (a friend joining does NOT flip an AI seat to HUMAN in US-148; that reconciliation is US-149). Endpoints on the existing unconditionally-mounted `routes/lobbies.py`: `join/{token}`, `GET /{id}/roster`, `POST /{id}/ready`, `POST /{id}/heartbeat`, `POST /{id}/lock`, `POST /{id}/kick/{member_id}`, `POST /{id}/transfer/{member_id}`, `GET /{id}/stream`. Authz helpers `_require_member_lobby` (404 for a non-member — a non-member cannot even probe existence) and `_require_host_lobby` (403 `not_host`). PRESENCE + AUTO-CANCEL lifecycle decisions live in a PURE module `api/lobby_presence.py` (data-in/data-out with an injected `now`, no clock/DB/IO): `is_present(member, now, stale_seconds)` (a member with no heartbeat falls back to `joined_at`), `stale_member_ids(...)`, `should_auto_cancel(lobby_updated_at, members, now, idle_seconds, stale_seconds)` (idle = `updated_at` older than idle window OR host-abandoned = no present member), `roster_view(...) -> [MemberView{member_id,is_host,ready,present}]` (the IDENTITY-BLIND roster shape — NO principal_id, NO seat_kind, NO per-seat human/AI map). The impure `_reconcile_lifecycle` in the route loads rows, calls the pure decider with `datetime.now(UTC)`, and applies eviction/CLOSED transition; it runs on every read (get/roster). The pure module coerces SQLite-naive `DateTime(timezone=True)` back to UTC-aware via a local `_as_aware` (same gotcha as US-127/131/136) — comparing the naive stored `joined_at`/`last_seen_at` against an aware `now` raises TypeError otherwise. The member-scoped state SSE channel `api/lobby_state.py::stream_lobby_state(session_factory, lobby_id, config=, clock=time.monotonic)` mirrors the US-133 live-tail shape: a fresh short-lived `async with session_factory() as session` per poll (no long-held session — friend lobbies sit open), an initial `lobby_state` snapshot frame then re-emit on any change (status/roster/ready/presence diff via `json.dumps(..., sort_keys=True)` comparison), keep-alive `: keep-alive` comment after `heartbeat_ms` idle, and close on a non-OPEN/LOCKED status (LAUNCHED/CLOSED/vanished) or `idle_timeout_ms` of no change. Timing injected via `LobbyStreamConfig(poll_ms, heartbeat_ms, idle_timeout_ms, stale_seconds)` from settings (`padrino_lobby_stream_*` + `padrino_lobby_presence_stale_seconds`); tests flip `PADRINO_LOBBY_STREAM_IDLE_TIMEOUT_MS=10` + `PADRINO_LOBBY_STREAM_POLL_MS=1` + `get_settings.cache_clear()` so the snapshot-then-close stream returns immediately and `resp.text` reads the full finite body. GOTCHA: `core.composition.CompositionSummary` is a `TypedDict` (a plain dict), NOT a pydantic model — use `dict(composition)`, not `.model_dump()`, in the SSE frame. KEY ANONYMITY: the roster/state surfaces return ONLY `member_id/is_host/ready/present` per member + counts-only `composition` — the test walks the JSON forbidding `{seat_kind, principal_id, agent_build_id, is_human, seats}` so no per-seat human/AI map can leak. New settings: `padrino_lobby_presence_stale_seconds` (60), `padrino_lobby_idle_cancel_seconds` (1800), `padrino_lobby_stream_poll_ms` (1000) / `_heartbeat_ms` (15000) / `_idle_timeout_ms` (300000). Test pattern (`tests/api/test_lobby_invite_presence.py`): mint two guest tokens via `POST /human/guest`, create a lobby, read its `invite_token` from `GET /lobbies/{id}`, join the friend; force presence staleness by writing `member.last_seen_at = now - 1h` directly in the DB then asserting the next host roster read evicts the friend; force idle auto-cancel by dragging `lobby.updated_at` 2h back then asserting status CLOSED. - Authenticated human action channel (US-134): a human submits a structured `Action {type, target?}` (exactly `core/engine/actions.Action`) for their OWN seat over `POST /human/games/{game_id}/actions` (on the existing unconditionally-mounted human router). The impure shell `api/human_actions.py::submit_action(session, *, game_id, principal_id, action, idempotency_key, now)` (1) resolves the caller's seat via `GameSeat.occupant_principal_id == principal_id` (no seat -> 403 `wrong_seat` — a human may act ONLY for the seat they occupy); (2) loads the event rows (`events_repo.list_events`) and recovers the deterministic `GameState` by reusing `runner.human_durability.replay_state_from_rows` (renamed from the private `_replay_state_from_rows` so the action channel shares the SAME verified-replay path as durability — it re-seals + verifies the hash chain); (3) validates against the PURE `legal_actions_for(state, core_seat)` for `format_phase_id(state.current_phase)`: action.type not in `allowed_action_types` -> 409 (`out_of_phase` if the seat has NO legal types at all this phase, else `illegal_action`); a TARGETED type (VOTE/MAFIA_KILL/PROTECT/INVESTIGATE) with a missing/illegal target -> 409 `illegal_action`; a NOOP/ABSTAIN carrying a target -> 409. A terminal game -> 409. (4) Idempotency: `human_action_submissions` table unique on `(game_id, public_player_id, phase, idempotency_key)`; `get_by_idempotency_key` short-circuits a retry to `idempotent_replay=True` WITHOUT a second insert (no double-vote). The route gates on `enforce_consent` (US-130) BEFORE validating, and the request model uses `ConfigDict(extra="forbid")` so a stray chat field (`public_message`) is a 422 — the chat firewall holds (chat is the SEPARATE US-135 channel; only the structured Action reaches here). Validation reads ONLY the pure core; no mechanics in the shell. - Deterministic curated auto-fill + launch handoff (US-149): a host launches a LOCKED lobby; empty AI seats fill deterministically from the curated pool, then a real human-lane Game + GameSeat rows are materialized. TWO halves: (1) PURE `core/lobby/autofill.py::autofill_empty_seats(*, lobby_seed, empty_seat_indices, reserved_build_ids, curated_roster) -> AutoFillAssignment{seat_index: build_id_str}` — dedupes the roster preserving order, DROPS any build already reserved on a pre-picked seat (no duplicate model in one game), raises `NotEnoughCuratedModelsError(empty_seats, pool_size)` when the available pool < empty seats, then `SeededRng(f"autofill:{lobby_seed}").shuffle(available)` and zips onto the seats sorted by index. Seat-index input order does NOT affect the result (sorted internally), so determinism is purely seed-driven. Imports ONLY SeededRng -> the `tests/core/test_purity.py` firewall covers a new `core/lobby/` package automatically (a bare `__init__.py` re-export is fine). (2) IMPURE `api/lobby_launch.py::launch_lobby(session, *, lobby_id) -> LaunchResult{game_id, created}`: idempotent/single-fire — an already-LAUNCHED lobby returns its existing game_id with `created=False` and writes NOTHING; otherwise requires status==LOCKED (else `LobbyNotLaunchableError`). It resolves reserved/empty AI lobby seats, runs autofill (`NotEnoughCuratedModelsError -> AutoFillPoolError`), derives `game_seed = sha256("game:"+lobby_seed)` (a DISTINCT namespace from the autofill seed), and CRUCIALLY assigns roles via the SAME pure `assign_roles(game_seed, ruleset)` the runner uses — so the GameSeat rows written now (role/faction/public_player_id P01..P0N by seat_index) AGREE with the `RolesAssigned` event the game later emits. This matters because the runner's `_persist_roles_assigned` SKIPS its own seat backfill when any seat lacks an agent_build (human games carry `agent_builds={}`), so the launch-handoff seats ARE the canonical seats. HUMAN lobby seats -> GameSeat(seat_kind=HUMAN, occupant_principal_id from the member's principal, agent_build_id=None); AI seats -> GameSeat(seat_kind=AI, agent_build_id=prepick-or-autofilled). The Game is gauntlet-less (gauntlet_id=None) so the benchmark scheduler (which claims via Gauntlet rows) can NEVER pick it up, and the presence of a HUMAN seat is EXACTLY what makes `runner.human_lane.list_human_lane_games` (US-132) claim it. `game.identity_mode` is copied from the lobby. Curated roster (v1) = every ACTIVE AgentBuild whose PromptVersion targets the lobby's ruleset, ordered (created_at, id) — a dedicated `human_eligible` flag/pool is deferred to US-151. Segregation holds free: the human lane runs `run_game(..., ranked=False)` with `agent_builds={}`, so `_should_apply_ratings` fails closed -> ZERO scientific Rating/RatingEvent rows. Route `POST /lobbies/{id}/launch` is host-only (`_require_host_lobby` -> 403/404), 409 `lobby_not_locked` / `autofill_pool_exhausted`, returns `LaunchResponse{lobby_id, game_id, status, created}`. Tests: `tests/core/test_lobby_autofill.py` (purity/determinism/seat-order-invariance/seed-sensitivity/reserved-exclusion/pool-too-small/dup-roster) + `tests/api/test_lobby_launch.py` (materializes 1 HUMAN + 6 AI distinct-build seats with full P01..P07 roster, game is gauntlet-less + on the human lane via `list_human_lane_games`, idempotent second call writes no second game, requires LOCKED + host + session, pool-too-small 409, zero scientific rating rows). The launch test seeds the curated pool with N active builds sharing one ModelConfig/PromptVersion(ruleset=mini7_v1) — `_create_and_lock` creates a lobby then POSTs `/lock` before launching.

- End-to-end human-spine smoke test (US-157): ONE default-suite test (`tests/integration/test_human_game_e2e.py`, NO `@pytest.mark.integration` marker so it runs under `-m "not integration"` — the integration dir is NOT auto-marked; the marker is applied per-test) drives the WHOLE human lane through REAL HTTP: guest create+consent (`/human/guest` cookie via `SimpleCookie` over set-cookie + `/human/consent`), `POST /lobbies` (host = lobby seat 0 = public_player_id P01 = the ONLY HUMAN seat in a default lobby; a guest `join/{invite_token}` adds a LobbyMember but NO playable HUMAN seat in v1), ready/lock/`launch` (curated auto-fill materializes the Game+GameSeat rows), then the game is driven by `run_game(..., ranked=False, persistence=GamePersistence(agent_builds={}, league_id=None))` with a `SeatMultiplexAdapter` mixing a `HumanAdapter` on P01 and `_ScriptedSeatAdapter`(DeterministicMockAdapter slice) on the AI seats. Post on the first `"_DISCUSSION_" in phase and not chat_sent[0]`. - Disconnect grace + silent AI takeover (US-150): a dropped human gets a short reconnect grace window; on expiry a curated AI silently takes the seat so the game continues, invisibly in anonymous mode. TWO modules, no schema change, no new deps. (1) PURE `core/disconnect.py` (data-in/data-out with an INJECTED `now` — never reads a clock): `SeatPresence{public_player_id, connected, disconnected_at}` + `is_within_grace(presence, *, now, grace_seconds)` (connected -> always within; disconnected within window -> reconnectable; a disconnected seat with NO drop instant treated as just-dropped) + `seats_past_grace(presences, *, now, grace_seconds) -> [seat_id]` (the disconnected seats whose window expired, in input order — a reconnect BEFORE expiry flips `connected=True` so the seat is never listed: "reconnect returns the seat") + `project_presence_for_viewer(presences, *, viewer_seat_id, identity_mode) -> [{seat_id, connected}]` (the IDENTITY-BLIND presence frame: in ANONYMOUS mode — the fail-closed default via `observation_privacy.is_anonymous`, so None coerces anonymous — it carries ONLY the viewer's OWN seat; other seats' presence/reconnecting state is NEVER exposed because an AI never disconnects, so any per-seat presence signal would out a human; TRANSPARENT may show all; each entry is `{seat_id, connected}` ONLY — never a drop timestamp or human/AI marker). `core/disconnect.py` imports `datetime` for pure grace ARITHMETIC (timedelta only) — add it to `tests/core/test_purity.py::ALLOWED_FORBIDDEN_IMPORTS` ("disconnect.py": frozenset({"datetime"})) EXACTLY like `scheduling/__init__.py`; the `test_allowed_datetime_modules_make_no_wallclock_calls` guard then enforces no `.now()/.utcnow()/.today()` (the module uses `value.replace(tzinfo=UTC)` for the SQLite-naive coercion — `replace` is not a wall-clock attr). (2) IMPURE `runner/disconnect_takeover.py::take_over_seat(*, mux, event_log, state, seat_id, replacement_adapter, replacement_agent_build_ref, reason="disconnect_grace_expired") -> TakeoverResult{event, replaced_adapter}`: REUSES US-139's `SeatMultiplexAdapter.swap_seat(seat, adapter)` (rebinds the dispatch table between ticks, returns the replaced human adapter, KeyError on an unknown seat — a takeover replaces an existing occupant) + US-122's `SeatTakenOver` event appended to the hash-chained `EventLog` with `day`/`phase` read from `state.current_phase` (pure logical values via `core.observations.format_phase_id` — NO wall clock/random in the payload). The takeover is REVEAL-ONLY: `SeatTakenOver` is SYSTEM-visibility so it NEVER lands on a PUBLIC/live frame (no mid-game leak); it surfaces only at the endgame reveal where `reducer.compute_seat_provenance(typed_events)` derives HUMAN_THEN_AI for the seat (requires the seat marked seat_kind=HUMAN in RolesAssigned, i.e. the US-149 launch handoff). New setting `padrino_human_reconnect_grace_seconds: float = 90.0` (wall-clock value consumed only in the impure runner; the pure decision reads it as plain data). Test `tests/runner/test_disconnect_takeover.py` (12): pure grace decisions (connected always within, recent-within/old-past, seats_past_grace lists only expired, reconnect-returns-seat, naive-timestamp coercion); identity-blind projection (anonymous shows only viewer's own seat, None fails closed, other-seat reconnecting never exposed, transparent shows all); runner orchestration reuses the US-139 `_TakeoverMux` + `_FakeClock` + `make_town_win_script`: a HUMAN seat is taken over mid-DAY_1_VOTE (swap on the real mux, `seats_past_grace` decides), the game still reaches TOWN, no PUBLIC frame carries SeatTakenOver, the committed log (incl. the appended SeatTakenOver) replays bit-for-bit, and `take_over_seat` on a hand-built HUMAN-marked RolesAssigned+state yields a SYSTEM-visibility pure-data event + HUMAN_THEN_AI provenance + KeyError on an unknown seat.

## 2026-06-21T01:30 PDT - US-194
- State-cache: preserve full tamper-detection + complete cache adoption. Three findings closed.
- (1) Tamper detection: `EventLog.from_stored` now re-seals each cached body (`compute_event_hash(prev, body)` vs stored `event_hash`) and raises `ValueError` on mismatch — restoring the full-re-seal guarantee the old `replay_state_from_rows` gave. The US-168 read path (`resolve_current_human_state`) previously trusted the cached prefix bodies and only cross-checked the cached HEAD against the DB head row, so a tampered pre-head body (head hash intact) was served. `_parse_state_cache` already maps `ValueError`->None, so a tampered cache now falls back to the verified full DB replay (`used_cache=False`) rather than being silently served.
- (2) Complete adoption: `api/human_turing.py::submit_guess` switched from the separate `replay_state_from_rows(rows)` full replay to the shared `resolve_current_human_state(session, game_id)` cache path (None->404). One state-resolution path across action/chat/observation/turing.
- (3) No accidental cache wipe: `db/repositories/human_game_runtime.upsert` `state_cache` is now tri-state via a private `_Unset` sentinel — omit preserves an existing cache, dict replaces, explicit None clears. A future partial-update caller that does not manage the cache can no longer wipe it. The `human_lane.py` snapshotter still passes `state_cache=...` explicitly (unchanged).
- Test-first: `tests/core/test_event_log.py` (from_stored round-trip + tampered-pre-head-body detection + broken-pointer rejection); `tests/runner/test_human_state_cache_integrity.py` (cache tamper -> used_cache=False fallback; omit preserves; explicit None clears).

## 2026-06-21T00:10 PDT - US-192
- Made the human seat presence heartbeat race-safe. `db/repositories/human_seat_presence.py` `record_heartbeat` / `mark_disconnected` previously did read-then-insert with no DB-level upsert; two concurrent first heartbeats for one `(game_id, public_player_id)` both saw no row, both INSERTed, and the second violated `uq_human_seat_presence` -> IntegrityError -> 500 on the presence/observation/action path.
- Both now route through a new `_upsert_presence(...)` helper doing a dialect-aware `INSERT ... ON CONFLICT (game_id, public_player_id) DO UPDATE` (postgresql + sqlite branches, mirroring the chat-sidecar sequence counter). Every column is supplied explicitly because ORM defaults (`id`, `updated_at`) don't fire on a Core insert. A `_KEEP` sentinel preserves `last_seen_at` on a disconnect UPDATE (so the worker lane can measure the grace window) while still nulling it on a fresh disconnect INSERT — matching the prior semantics exactly. After the upsert the helper expires any stale identity-map instance and re-reads so callers/tests get a managed ORM row.
- Test-first: `tests/db/test_human_seat_presence_upsert.py` fires 8 simultaneous heartbeats (and a mixed heartbeat/disconnect burst) for one seat across separate sessions behind an `asyncio.Event` barrier and asserts no IntegrityError + a single coherent row; a third test checks heartbeat -> disconnect -> reconnect transitions preserve/clear `last_seen_at`/`disconnected_at` correctly.

## 2026-06-19T21:00 - US-138
- Human-aware tick + symmetric fixed release delay. The tick must wait on slow humans under human-friendly deadlines and release ALL public messages (human AND AI) on the same fixed delay, so message timing cannot out a seat (decision 5, simplified: fixed delay, NO seeded jitter / multi-message windows in v1; AI messages wait in the buffer too).

Wraps the UNCHANGED `runner/tick.run_tick` (no tick.py contract change) with `timeout_s=config.phase_deadline_seconds` so a slow human (HumanAdapter resolves its own deadline) is coerced to a safe action by the same hard barrier as a slow LLM, then holds the phase's public messages and releases them after ONE fixed `release_delay_seconds` measured on the INJECTED clock — every message in the phase gets an IDENTICAL `released_at` (no per-side timing signal). Public messages gated to DAY_DISCUSSION/DAY_VOTE, collected in seat order. `HumanTickConfig {phase_deadline_seconds, release_delay_seconds}` (plain data), `ReleasedMessage {seat_id, text, released_at}`, `HumanTickResult {responses, released_messages, settled_at}`. ## 2026-06-19T01:00 - US-114
- Scheduler claim hardening: `claim_oldest_pending` (in `db/repositories/gauntlets.py`, the runner/scheduler claim path called at `runner/scheduler.py:300`) now applies `SELECT ... FOR UPDATE SKIP LOCKED` on PostgreSQL only. Implemented via `if session.get_bind().dialect.name == "postgresql": stmt = stmt.with_for_update(skip_locked=True)` between building the ordered-limit-1 select and executing it. SQLite path is unchanged (no `FOR UPDATE`); the docstring documents that SQLite is single-writer so row-lock skipping is neither needed nor possible.
- Created `tests/db/test_scheduler_claim_skip_locked.py` (2 tests, `@pytest.mark.postgres`, testcontainers `postgres:17-alpine`, skipped without docker): two concurrent claimers over 2 PENDING rows receive DISTINCT gauntlet ids (never the same); two concurrent claimers over 1 PENDING row -> one gets the row + the other gets None (proving the loser SKIPs the row-locked row rather than blocking/re-reading it). Both run each claim in its own session+commit so the asyncio.gather races real concurrent transactions; verified GREEN locally against a live container.
- Files changed: `src/padrino/db/repositories/gauntlets.py`, `tests/db/test_scheduler_claim_skip_locked.py`, `ralph/prd.json`, `ralph/progress.txt`
- Gates (all GREEN): `ruff check .`, `ruff format --check .` (304 files), `mypy src tests` (277 files), `pytest -m "not integration"` -> 1666 passed / 29 skipped. The new postgres-marked tests pass standalone against a real container (`pytest tests/db/test_scheduler_claim_skip_locked.py` -> 2 passed).
- **Learnings for future iterations:**
  - Dialect-conditional SQL in a repo helper: `session.get_bind().dialect.name` returns `"postgresql"` / `"sqlite"`; gate `with_for_update(skip_locked=True)` on it so the same helper stays cross-dialect (SQLite raises/ignores `FOR UPDATE` depending on driver — just omit it). Same `bind.dialect.name` switch pattern already used in `api/rate_limit_store.py`.
  - To actually exercise SKIP LOCKED in a test you MUST run each claimer in its own `factory()` session and `commit()`, then `asyncio.gather` them — a single shared session serializes and never demonstrates the skip. The fixture (`postgres_url` session-scoped container + per-test `postgres_engine` drop/create) is copied from `tests/db/test_dialect_portability.py`.

## 2026-06-19T00:00 - US-113
- Operational alerting machinery: webhook notifier + condition-transition alert rules.
- New `src/padrino/observability/alerts.py` with `AlertNotifier` (async): always emits a structured `alert.fired` log; POSTs the alert as JSON to `padrino_alert_webhook_url` via an injected `httpx.AsyncClient` (no-op when URL/client unset). The core property is fire-once-per-transition: `fire(key, **details)` only POSTs when the key flips inactive->active and returns False (suppressed) while the condition persists; `resolve(key)` re-arms it. Per-key running counters (`increment`/`reset_counter`) carry the consecutive-admission-denial streak across ticks. `build_alert_notifier(settings)` constructs a real owned client when the URL is set, else log-only.
- Added `EVENT_ALERT_FIRED = "alert.fired"` to `observability/events.py`.
- New settings: `padrino_alert_webhook_url: str | None = None`, `padrino_alert_webhook_timeout_s: float = 5.0`, `padrino_scheduler_heartbeat_stale_seconds: float = 120.0`, `padrino_admission_denied_streak_threshold: int = 5`.
- Wired alerts into the EXISTING continuous-matchmaking tick (`scheduler/continuous_matchmaking.py`, optional `notifier` param): `scheduler.heartbeat.stale` (latest `scheduler_heartbeats.latest_beat` older than the window), `moderation.guard.unavailable` (guard None while matchmaking enabled), `spend.cap.reached` (admit() reason == spend_cap_reached), `admission.denied.streak` (N consecutive denials; reset + resolved on the next successful admission). Threaded through `scheduler/bootstrap.py` and constructed in `cli.py serve` via `build_alert_notifier`.
- New Prometheus alert-rules file `docs/deployment/alert-rules.yml` (4 rules, one per webhook condition) derived from existing `/metrics` series; ships with the deploy config.
- Created `tests/observability/test_alerts.py` (20 tests, httpx MockTransport, no integration marker): fire posts JSON + de-dups until resolve; log-only when URL unset; delivery error never propagates; counter helpers; each tick trigger (stale heartbeat / guard-none / spend-cap / denial-streak) fires exactly once per transition; the alert-rules YAML parses and has one rule per alert key. Reuses the shared `session_factory` conftest fixture.
- Files changed: `src/padrino/observability/alerts.py`, `src/padrino/observability/events.py`, `src/padrino/settings.py`, `src/padrino/scheduler/continuous_matchmaking.py`, `src/padrino/scheduler/bootstrap.py`, `src/padrino/cli.py`, `docs/deployment/alert-rules.yml`, `tests/observability/test_alerts.py`, `ralph/prd.json`, `ralph/progress.txt`
- Gates (all GREEN): `ruff check .`, `ruff format --check .` (303 files), `mypy src tests` (276 files), `pytest -m "not integration"` -> 1663 passed / 29 skipped.
- **Learnings for future iterations:**
  - Alert de-duplication = a per-key active-flag state machine on the notifier, NOT a per-tick check. `fire()` flips inactive->active and returns whether it actually transitioned; the matching `resolve()` (called when the condition clears) re-arms it. This is the only way to satisfy "fires exactly once per condition transition (no spam every tick)".
  - The continuous-matchmaking tick is the single seam where all four conditions are observable in one place (it already calls `admit()` and holds the guard), so wiring the notifier there (optional param, threaded from bootstrap/cli) keeps the alert logic out of the pure paths and out of the spend governor/admission modules themselves.
  - httpx MockTransport (`httpx.AsyncClient(transport=httpx.MockTransport(handler))`) is the canonical no-network webhook test: the handler records `json.loads(request.content)` and returns `httpx.Response(200, ...)`. A handler that raises `httpx.ConnectError` proves delivery failures are swallowed.

  - `/public/recent` (the only surface that reads local `Game` rows AND could carry an ingested game's id) gained an exclusion: a new `_excluded_game_ids(session)` helper resolves the unverified ingested `game_id`s to local `Game.id` UUIDs and the index query/count add `Game.id.notin_(excluded)`. `game_id` is the string form of `Game.id` (see `export/bundle.py:433` `game_id=str(game.id)`), so the diff is exact.
  - `/public/ladder` + `/public/models/leaderboard` read the local `ratings` table only; ingest writes ZERO `Rating` rows, so unverified (and verified) ingests are absent there by construction — asserted, not modified.
- New repo helper `ingested_games_repo.unverified_game_ids(session) -> set[str]` (filters `verification_status != VERIFIED`) is the single source of truth for the exclusion set.
- Created `tests/api/test_public_excludes_unverified.py` (5 tests): seeds one house game (+ranked Rating), one verified ingest (+matching local Game), one unverified ingest (+matching local Game); asserts the unverified game/entity is absent from recent / leaderboard / ladder / model-rollup, present where expected, and STILL retrievable on the detail surface `GET /public/games/{id}` with `verification_status="unverified"`.
- Files changed: `src/padrino/db/repositories/ingested_games.py`, `src/padrino/api/routes/public.py`, `tests/api/test_public_excludes_unverified.py`, `ralph/prd.json`, `ralph/progress.txt`
- Gates (all GREEN): `ruff check .`, `ruff format --check .` (301 files), `mypy src tests` (274 files), `pytest -m "not integration"` -> 1647 passed / 29 skipped.
- **Learnings for future iterations:**
  - There are TWO distinct "public" data families: (1) the federated leaderboard reads the `ingested_games` table directly (`compute_public_leaderboard`), already verified-filtered; (2) recent/live/ladder/model-rollup read the LOCAL `games`/`ratings` tables, which ingest never populates. The only cross-over risk is `game_id == str(Game.id)` letting an ingested row shadow a local Game row in the recent index — that is the one place the explicit `notin_` filter is load-bearing.
  - To exclude unverified-ingest games from a `Game`-table query: `excluded = await _excluded_game_ids(session)` (resolves string `game_id`s to `uuid.UUID`, dropping malformed ones) then `Game.id.notin_(excluded)` guarded by `if excluded` (an empty `notin_([])` is a SQL no-op but the guard keeps the query clean and avoids dialect edge cases).

## Codebase Patterns

- `create_app(public_surface_only=True)` (or `PADRINO_PUBLIC_SURFACE_ONLY=true`) builds the internet-facing process: only the public router + health router are mounted; private routers and `/metrics` are NOT registered, so private prefixes 404 (route absent), never 401/403. The flag resolves like the other `create_app` knobs: explicit kwarg wins, else `settings.padrino_public_surface_only`. Note `scheduled_gauntlets_router` carries BOTH private CRUD and one public route (`/public/scheduled-gauntlets`); gating the whole router (per AC) drops that public route too — the must-work public surface is the enumerated set (`/public/live`, `/public/recent`, `/public/ladder`, `/public/games/{id}/live`).
- `src/padrino/public/` is the new module for Wave 7 public surface. Start each new public module here.
- The public spectator website (`web/dashboard`) must call ONLY `/public/*` endpoints from any nav- or URL-reachable page (it ships against the public-surface-only API). To get a league_id without the private `/gauntlets`, chain public reads: `/public/recent` -> `GET /public/games/{id}.league_id`. The e2e smoke spawn sets `PADRINO_PUBLIC_LEADERBOARD_ANONYMOUS=true` (`tests/e2e/global-setup.ts`) so keyless `/public/*` reads work; the smoke harness does NOT seed broadcastable RECENT games, so `/public/recent` + `/public/live` are empty there (only `/public/ladder` has data from the gauntlet's ratings).
- `padrino.core.spectator_projection.project_event_for_spectator` is the identity-blind filter for PUBLIC events; always build on top of it rather than reimplementing visibility filtering.
- `padrino.core.observation_privacy.FORBIDDEN_PAYLOAD_KEYS` is the canonical deny list for identity/role/faction leaks — shared across spectator, ranked-observation, and public_event_v1.
- Golden-file tests live in `tests/public/fixtures/` as JSON. The test loads the file and diffs computed output against stored expected — any schema drift fails the test until the golden file is updated consciously.
- `gauntlets.claim_oldest_pending` is the single scheduler claim seam (called from `runner/scheduler.py`). It applies `with_for_update(skip_locked=True)` ONLY when `session.get_bind().dialect.name == "postgresql"`, making horizontal scaling safe on Postgres (two replicas never double-claim) while leaving SQLite single-writer. For any new dialect-conditional SQL in a repo, branch on `session.get_bind().dialect.name`. To test cross-replica DB concurrency, give each claimer its own `factory()` session + `commit()` and `asyncio.gather` them (a shared session serializes and proves nothing); reuse the testcontainers `postgres_url`/`postgres_engine` fixtures from `tests/db/test_dialect_portability.py` under `@pytest.mark.postgres`.
- `padrino.observability.alerts.AlertNotifier` is the canonical operational-alert seam: `await notifier.fire(key, **details)` is fire-once-per-transition (de-duped via a per-key active flag) and `notifier.resolve(key)` re-arms it; it always logs `alert.fired` and POSTs JSON to `padrino_alert_webhook_url` when set. Build it with `build_alert_notifier(settings)`. The matchmaking tick (`run_continuous_matchmaking_tick`, optional `notifier=` param, threaded from `scheduler/bootstrap.py` + `cli.py`) is where spend-cap / stale-heartbeat / guard-unavailable / admission-denial-streak conditions are wired. Add new operator alerts here, never as raw per-tick logs. Test with `httpx.AsyncClient(transport=httpx.MockTransport(handler))` — no network, no integration marker.

  - `dict.fromkeys(roster, 0)` avoids ruff C420 (unnecessary dict comprehension for iterable with fixed value).

  - `sorted(shuffled, key=lambda a: play_counts[a])` — shuffle first for tie-breaking, then stable-sort by count — is the canonical pattern for deterministic least-played selection.

- Files changed: `web/dashboard/src/routes/watch/[id]/+page.svelte`, `web/dashboard/tests/e2e/watch.spec.ts`
- **Learnings for future iterations:**
  - Playwright can mock SSE by fulfilling with `contentType: 'text/event-stream'` and a complete SSE body string; browser EventSource parses it correctly and fires all events.
  - Abort reconnect requests with `route.abort('failed')` in the route handler (after first fulfillment) to prevent duplicate events from re-delivering the same SSE body.
  - `sse = false; prerender = false` in `+layout.ts` means the whole app is a pure SPA — no SSR guards needed for browser APIs like `EventSource`.

## Codebase Patterns
- docker-compose split topology (US-119): the public/private boundary is encoded as (1) a separate `public-api` service with PADRINO_PUBLIC_SURFACE_ONLY=true publishing the only edge port, (2) the full `api`/scheduler/postgres publishing NO host ports and living only on the `internal` network, (3) two compose networks `edge` (public-api + dashboard) and `internal` (everything). The dashboard is built against `http://public-api:8000` (VITE_PADRINO_API_BASE_URL). test_compose_v2.py asserts the graph by parsing the YAML (no containers) under `-m docker`.

## 2026-06-19 — US-137: HumanAdapter satisfies the LlmAdapter protocol
Files:
- src/padrino/llm/human_adapter.py (NEW): HumanAdapter implements the LlmAdapter Protocol. complete(observation) polls an injected PullAction source for buffered human input (the US-134 POST channel) every poll_interval_seconds until either a submission arrives or deadline_seconds elapses (measured on an injected monotonic clock). Legal submission -> AgentResponse verbatim (status ok); illegal type/target -> coerce_response_failure (status schema_violation); deadline miss -> coerce_response_failure (status provider_error). Legality reuses legal_actions (carried on the observation) with the same targeted/untargeted rules as api/human_actions.py. NO tick.py contract change.
- src/padrino/llm/observation_phase.py (NEW): promoted mock.py's private _phase_from_observation/_phase_kind_for into public phase_from_observation/phase_kind_for so HumanAdapter and DeterministicMock/NoopMock share one phase-id->Phase reconstruction for coercion.
- src/padrino/llm/mock.py: now imports phase_from_observation from observation_phase (behavior identical).
- tests/llm/test_human_adapter.py (NEW, 10 tests): protocol conformance, buffered-legal-resolve (polls+sleeps then resolves), timeout-coerce (ABSTAIN on DAY_VOTE, NOOP on NIGHT_ACTIONS), illegal-type/illegal-target/targetless-with-target coerce, legal-abstain passthrough, immediate-input-no-sleep. Clock + async sleep injected (FakeClock advances only on sleep) so tests are deterministic, no wall-clock.
- tests/public/test_broadcast_pipeline_e2e.py: updated import of the moved phase_kind_for helper.
- ralph/prd.json (passes:true), ralph/progress.txt
Notes:
- No migration; no new runtime deps. The adapter owns its deadline internally and returns a valid (coerced) AdapterResult so the runner's asyncio.wait_for tick barrier (US-138) stays unchanged.
- Avoided `# type: ignore`: _coerce's status param is typed AdapterStatus (imported from llm.adapter) so literal "schema_violation"/"provider_error" typecheck cleanly.
- Gates (all GREEN): ruff check ., ruff format --check . (361 files), mypy src tests (323 files), pytest -m "not integration" -> 1895 passed / 40 skipped.

## Codebase Patterns
- Block-before-release human chat moderation (US-140): the REAL verdict is `padrino.api.human_chat_moderation.RealtimeModerationHook` (implements the US-135 `ChatModerationHook` Protocol; replaces `StubPassModerationHook` as the channel default). Verdict order for ONE held message: (1) pure `public.moderation.deterministic_first_pass_message(text)` instant backstop — a hard-tier hit (`_TOXIC_PATTERNS`, sentinel `toxic_word`) is an immediate BLOCK and the async guard is NEVER called; (2) pure `core.agents.sanitizer.sanitize_visible_text` + pure `public.moderation.deterministic_span_mask(text)` (masks `_SOFT_MASK_PATTERNS`, sentinel `mask_word`, with same-length `*` runs) produce the SOFT_MASK release text; (3) async `MessageGuardAdapter.check_message` under `asyncio.wait_for(timeout_s)` — `False`->BLOCK, timeout/error->FALL BACK to the step-2 deterministic verdict (the game never halts), safe->ALLOW/SOFT_MASK. HARD-tier and soft-tier are SEPARATE pattern sets so SOFT_MASK is reachable (a hard hit blocks before span-mask runs). A BLOCK carries `cleaned_text=None` and is never released/chained/sidecar'd; ALLOW/SOFT_MASK route `cleaned_text` to the US-123 sidecar (raw never inline in a hashed payload). Rate limits: `submit_chat(rate_limit=RateLimitStore, per_principal_limit, per_game_phase_limit)` checks TWO keyed buckets (`human-chat:user:{pid}` and `human-chat:game-phase:{game}:{phase}`, both sha256-hashed) AFTER the idempotency check so a retry consumes no slot; over cap -> HTTPException 429 `chat_rate_limited`. The route pulls the store via `request.app.state.rate_limiter.store`. Settings: `padrino_rate_limit_human_chat_per_minute`, `padrino_rate_limit_human_chat_per_game_phase_per_minute`, `padrino_human_chat_guard_timeout_seconds`. Test the gate with a RECORDING guard stub (asserts `guard.seen == [...]`) to prove it actually saw the message (guards the Wave-7 vacuous-gate bug class).
- Human seat as an adapter (US-137): a human seat is driven through the EXACT same LlmAdapter contract as an LLM. HumanAdapter(pull_action=..., deadline_seconds, poll_interval_seconds, clock, sleep) polls a buffered-input source (the POST action channel) and returns an AdapterResult: legal->verbatim AgentResponse, illegal->coerce_response_failure(schema_violation), timeout->coerce_response_failure(provider_error). Legality is checked against observation.legal_actions (targeted types VOTE/MAFIA_KILL/PROTECT/INVESTIGATE need a legal target; NOOP/ABSTAIN must carry none) — the SAME rule as api/human_actions.py. Inject clock+sleep for deterministic deadline tests (FakeClock advances only when sleep is awaited). Reconstruct the core Phase for coercion via padrino.llm.observation_phase.phase_from_observation. This keeps the tick barrier contract unchanged (the adapter resolves its own deadline and never raises).

## Codebase Patterns (append)
- Identity-mode-aware projection (US-141): the canonical fail-closed coercion is `core.observation_privacy.coerce_identity_mode` / `is_anonymous` (string-based, no enum dep). Two reusable identity sets live in observation_privacy: `IDENTITY_MARKER_KEYS` (human-vs-AI + model/provider markers — the subset TRANSPARENT mode may disclose) and `FORBIDDEN_PAYLOAD_KEYS` (everything stripped in anonymous, incl. role/faction). Build a transparent strip-set as `FORBIDDEN_PAYLOAD_KEYS - IDENTITY_MARKER_KEYS` so role/faction/ratings stay hidden mid-game even when transparent. For a per-seat view, surface transparent identity as an explicit `identity_disclosure` block carrying ONLY model/human facts (never role/faction), and keep it `None` in anonymous mode. NOTE: observation_privacy imports Observation from observations, so observations must use a function-local import of is_anonymous to avoid a cycle.

Files:
- src/padrino/core/reveal.py (NEW, pure): the ONE canonical endgame reveal schema (the review found 5 divergent ad-hoc shapes). `SeatRevealInput` (shell-resolved data-in: public_player_id, seat_index, seat_kind, role, faction, alive, taken_over_at_phase, model) -> `project_seat_reveal` / `project_endgame_reveal` -> `SeatReveal` / `EndgameReveal` (frozen pydantic). Takeover provenance maps directly off SeatKind: AI->"AI", HUMAN->"HUMAN", AI_TAKEOVER->"HUMAN_THEN_AI"; missing/unknown kind fails closed to AI (never invents a human). `is_human` reflects who FINISHED the seat (AI_TAKEOVER reads is_human=False but keeps HUMAN_THEN_AI provenance). A human-held seat ALWAYS drops any supplied model (a human seat can never leak a model). Seats emitted sorted by seat_index for determinism. No clock/random/IO -> pure-core firewall clean.
- src/padrino/api/routes/public.py: `GET /public/games/{id}/reveal` (response_model=EndgameReveal). Terminal-gated on broadcast_state==RECENT (LIVE / HIDDEN / not-broadcastable / unknown -> 404 so the truth is never one event early); served even in ANONYMOUS mode (decision 11). Shell resolver `_resolve_seat_models(session, seats)` joins AgentBuild->ModelConfig->ModelProvider for each seat's FINISHING build (takeover_agent_build_id takes precedence over agent_build_id so an AI_TAKEOVER seat reveals the AI that actually finished it) and returns {agent_build_id: RevealModel}. winner pulled from game.terminal_result. Added to __all__.

- tests/api/test_endgame_reveal.py (NEW, 5 tests): LIVE/HIDDEN/unknown -> 404; terminal RECENT returns full per-seat truth (human/AI, role, faction, exact model via provider/model_name/display_name, HUMAN_THEN_AI takeover w/ finishing model); reveal served in ANONYMOUS mode.

- No migration, no new deps (reuses the existing seat columns from US-121/122 + the AgentBuild->ModelConfig->ModelProvider chain). The reveal reads is_human/provenance straight off GameSeat.seat_kind + taken_over_at_phase (set by the launch-handoff/takeover stories), NOT from compute_seat_provenance event replay — equivalent and avoids a chain load on the read path.

## Codebase Patterns (append)
- Canonical endgame reveal (US-143): `core.reveal.project_endgame_reveal(*, game_id, ruleset_id, winner, seats: Iterable[SeatRevealInput]) -> EndgameReveal` is the SINGLE reveal schema — every reveal surface (API/frontend/exports) must consume it, never assemble its own per-seat truth. The pure layer takes shell-resolved `SeatRevealInput` (the impure route reads GameSeat rows + joins AgentBuild->ModelConfig->ModelProvider into a `RevealModel`); takeover provenance is derived purely from SeatKind (AI/HUMAN/AI_TAKEOVER -> AI/HUMAN/HUMAN_THEN_AI, fail-closed to AI). KEY for an AI_TAKEOVER seat: resolve the FINISHING model via `takeover_agent_build_id or agent_build_id` so the reveal shows the AI that actually finished. Terminal gating is the ROUTE's job (broadcast_state==RECENT else 404); the reveal is always served even in ANONYMOUS mode (decision 11) — anonymity hides identity DURING the game, the reveal is the post-terminal exception. Mirrors the composition-disclosure split (US-142): pure producer in core, thin DB-resolution shell in the route.

## 2026-06-19 — US-144: Spot-the-AI guess + pure scorer + personal stat
Files:
- src/padrino/core/turing/__init__.py + scoring.py (NEW, pure): `score_guess(*, guesser_public_id, guess: Mapping[str,str], truth: Mapping[str,bool]) -> GuessScore`. truth maps each seat's public_player_id to whether a human FINISHED it (AI_TAKEOVER -> False, i.e. counts as AI, matching the canonical reveal). guess maps every OTHER seat to GUESS_HUMAN/GUESS_AI. The guesser's own seat is excluded even if present. Raises ValueError for an unknown seat / invalid label / incomplete guess (a non-guesser seat left unguessed). GuessScore is frozen pydantic (guesser_public_id, total, correct, accuracy). accuracy is a DECIMAL STRING not a float (hard rule 4: no floats in core) — whole ratios render "0"/"1", fractional use the deterministic float repr via `_accuracy_string`. No clock/random/IO -> pure-core firewall clean. NO leaderboard: only ever one guesser's personal stat.
- src/padrino/db/models.py: `HumanTuringGuess` (game_id FK CASCADE, guesser_public_id, guess JSON {public_player_id:label}, total, correct, accuracy str, created_at) UNIQUE(game_id, guesser_public_id) — exactly one guess per guesser.

- src/padrino/api/routes/human.py: POST /human/games/{id}/turing-guess (consent-gated; TuringGuessSubmission.guess: dict[str, Literal["HUMAN","AI"]], extra='forbid' — no action/chat fields) + GET /human/games/{id}/turing-guess (gates the viewer's own accuracy behind their submitted guess: 404 guess_not_found before, the personal stat after).

Terminality for the guess flow comes from the REPLAYED state (consistent with the action channel), not from game.status.

## Codebase Patterns (append)
- Post-terminal personal-stat channel (US-144): a thin post-game step over the EXISTING human channel (POST + GET under /human/games/{id}/...), NOT a new FSM phase. Pattern: pure producer in core (core/turing/scoring.py — no clock/random/IO; emits accuracy as a DECIMAL STRING, never a float, so it crosses the core boundary cleanly), thin impure shell (api/human_turing.py) that resolves the caller's seat via GameSeat.occupant_principal_id (->403 wrong_seat), requires terminality from the REPLAYED state (state.terminal_result is not None, ->409), builds the seat truth from GameSeat.seat_kind==HUMAN (AI_TAKEOVER counts as AI, matching the reveal), scores, and persists once-per-guesser (UNIQUE(game_id, guesser_public_id); a re-submission returns the stored row — never re-score). GATING a personal result behind an action: a GET endpoint returns the stored stat or 404 if the prerequisite (the submitted guess) is absent — the reveal hands out the accuracy ONLY after the viewer submits their own guess. NO leaderboard in v1 (decision 6): the scorer only ever takes ONE guesser + the truth, never a cross-player ranking.
