## Codebase Patterns (append)
- Per-human play-history stats (US-145): mirror the scientific analytics split — pure producer in `analytics.deterministic` (`compute_participant_stats(events, participant_map)`; counts not floats so they sum across games, rates are @propertys), thin impure shell in `analytics.human_stats` (recompute-from-scratch rollup, idempotent under a UNIQUE key, upsert). KEY segregation pattern: a "human-lane" seat is `seat_kind in {HUMAN, AI_TAKEOVER}` AND `occupant_principal_id is not None`; building the `{public_player_id -> principal_id}` map ONLY from such seats makes a scientific (AI-only) game produce an empty map -> ZERO human rows by construction (no separate guard needed), matching the runner.human_lane lane-membership rule. Detection accuracy = fraction of a seat's `DetectiveResultDelivered` events whose `finding == "MAFIA"` (structured event only). The pure extractor's `participant_map` values are opaque (typed `Mapping[str, object]`) — only the keys select seats, so the same fn takes str or UUID principal ids.

## 2026-06-19 — US-151: Cost governance: caps + throttle-not-kill breaker
Files:
- src/padrino/economics/human_cost_governance.py (NEW, impure economics shell): per-user/day admission caps keyed on the human PRINCIPAL (OAuth account principal else the guest principal derived from the hashed guest token — the Principal row IS the unified key, so "hashed guest token" resolves to principal_id upstream in auth). `admit_human(session, settings, *, principal_id, action, now=None) -> HumanAdmitDecision` gates create/join/launch in order: global breaker -> daily inference-$ cap -> the action's daily count cap (games for create/launch via ACTION_CREATE/ACTION_LAUNCH, joins for ACTION_JOIN). `price_turn_usd(...)` prefers LiteLLM response_cost, else the fallback per-1K token-price table (model key then "default"; missing tokens -> 0). `human_eligible_pool(session, ruleset_id)` is the single curated source (ACTIVE builds for the ruleset, ordered created_at,id). Breaker: `lobby_breaker_open(session, settings, lobby)` = global breaker OR per-lobby accrued >= cap (READ-ONLY: NEVER mutates game/seat — throttles new turns, lets active game finish); `global_breaker_open` over cumulative human-lane spend (games with a HUMAN GameSeat).

- Cost is attributed to a principal via the games they occupy a GameSeat in (LlmCall.game_id -> GameSeat.occupant_principal_id), reusing the US-145 human-lane membership rule; daily windows use the injected `now` (no clock read in the module), mirroring economics/admission.py.
- The breaker is intentionally READ-ONLY: it returns a bool the api/runner shell consults before opening a NEW lobby or issuing a NEW LLM turn. The test asserts an open breaker leaves the active game's status/seats byte-untouched — encoding the rejected "AI-only continuation boots humans" anti-pattern directly.

## Codebase Patterns (append)
- Human cost governance (US-151): per-user caps key on the human PRINCIPAL (the Principal row unifies OAuth-account and guest identities, so "OAuth account else hashed guest token" is already principal_id by the time admission runs). Attribute inference $ to a principal via games they occupy (LlmCall.game_id -> GameSeat.occupant_principal_id, same membership rule as US-145 human-lane stats); a "human-lane game" = a game with >=1 GameSeat seat_kind=HUMAN. A circuit breaker for "throttle-not-kill" is a READ-ONLY predicate (`*_breaker_open(...) -> bool`) the impure shell consults BEFORE a NEW lobby/turn — it NEVER mutates a game/seat, and the canonical test asserts an open breaker leaves the active RUNNING game + its HUMAN seat byte-untouched (encodes the rejected "AI-only continuation boots humans" anti-pattern). Token pricing: prefer LiteLLM response_cost, fall back to a settings per-1K table keyed by model with a "default" catch-all (missing token counts -> 0, never crash). Forward-compat enum-on-a-row: add FundingSource {PLATFORM default, BYOK_OWNER, SPONSOR_POOL} now (dormant) so no later migration is needed when BYOK/sponsor ship.
- Wiring a governance predicate into the impure shell (US-151 retry 2): the READ-ONLY library is only meaningful once CALLED at the real admission/issuance points. (1) Endpoint admission: each lobby handler (create/join/launch in api/routes/lobbies.py) calls a shared `_enforce_admission(request, session, *, principal_id, action)` BEFORE writing rows; it reads settings via `getattr(request.app.state, "auth_settings", None) or get_settings()` (so a test pins tiny caps by overriding `app.state.auth_settings`) and raises HTTP 429 with `detail=decision.reason` on denial. principal_id comes straight from `require_human`'s ctx (already OAuth-account-else-guest). An IDEMPOTENT re-join (already a member) is exempt — it writes no row, so it consumes no slot. (2) "Stop new LLM turns, let active games finish" maps cleanly onto the human-lane runner: a not-yet-claimed game has issued ZERO turns, so `run_human_lane` simply SKIPS dispatching new games while `global_breaker_open` is True (gate the `pending` list per tick) — already-dispatched asyncio tasks keep running to completion, so the breaker throttles without ever killing/booting. Inject `settings=` into `run_human_lane` for deterministic test thresholds. Tests must drive the REAL endpoints/runner (tests/api/test_lobby_admission.py + tests/runner/test_human_lane_isolation.py breaker tests), not the library in isolation, to prove enforcement.

## Codebase Patterns (append)
- Bundled static assets (US-152): ship pre-generated files under src/padrino/assets/<kind>/ with an `assets/__init__.py` package, add `src/padrino/assets/<kind>/**/*.<ext>` to `[tool.hatch.build.targets.wheel] artifacts` (same as US-052 prompt markdown), and read them at runtime via `importlib.resources.files("padrino.assets").joinpath(...).read_bytes()` (works from an installed wheel). The asset route validates path segments against a `[a-z0-9_]+` Path `pattern=` (blocks `/`/`.` traversal) AND validates the key against a PURE allowlist from the core (`sprite_keys_for_pack`) — never trust the filesystem alone — then serves with an immutable Cache-Control. Anonymity for a derived display asset belongs in ONE pure resolver (`core/sprites.resolve_seat_sprite`) gated by `observation_privacy.is_anonymous` (fail-closed): ANONYMOUS returns a role-agnostic archetype keyed only by a stable sha256(public_player_id) hash (no role/seat-kind input), so the sprite can never encode role or human/AI; only TRANSPARENT may surface a role-specific asset.

- web/dashboard/src/lib/api/liveClient.ts (NEW): `LiveClient` — the SSE-out half of the play spine. Consumes the live-tail stream and reconnects BY SEQUENCE: tracks the highest delivered sequence, reopens via buildUrl(after=cursor), and DROPS any frame whose sequence <= cursor so a resume overlap is gap-free AND duplicate-free. `EventSource` is injected (LiveEventSource structural type + EventSourceFactory) so it is unit-testable with a fake. Also `newIdempotencyKey()` (crypto.randomUUID with a monotonic fallback) for the action/chat POST idempotency keys.
- web/dashboard/src/lib/api/playState.ts (NEW, pure reducer): `applyFrame(state, frame)`/`applyFrames` fold RELEASED public_event_v1 frames into a PlayState {phase, seats[], votes, chat[], winner, terminal}. Derives chat from PublicMessageSubmitted, latest vote per voter (cleared on phase change), seat-dead from PlayerEliminated, winner from GameTerminated. Resume-overlap frames (seq <= lastSequence) are a no-op returning the SAME reference. Pure/framework-free so it is exhaustively unit-tested without the runes runtime.
- web/dashboard/src/lib/playSession.svelte.ts (NEW, Svelte 5 runes): thin reactive shell wiring `LiveClient` -> `applyFrame` into `$state`, exposing board/votes/chat/winner/terminal as getters. The reducer is the tested core; this file is type-checked by svelte-check.
- web/dashboard/src/lib/clientStore.svelte.ts: the global client store gains a `humanSession` $state + `setHumanSession(enabled)` toggling the client's credential mode (cookie is never readable here).
- web/dashboard/src/lib/api/index.ts: re-export liveClient + playState.
- Tests (vitest, parallel the existing client tests): client.test.ts +10 cases (credential mode, action/chat POST + body, guess submit/read, composition+reveal, lobby create/join/ready/launch, guest mint + stats ruleset gating, error detail, URL builders); liveClient.test.ts (NEW, in-order delivery + cursor, reconnect-by-sequence dropping overlap dupes, no-reopen-after-close, non-JSON ignored, distinct idempotency keys); playState.test.ts (NEW, chat feed, vote tracking + phase-change clear, eliminated seat, terminal winner, idempotent resume folding).
- ralph/prd.json (passes:true), ralph/progress.txt
Notes:
- No `/human/stats` HTTP route exists yet (US-145 only PERSISTS the human_player_stats aggregate; no endpoint was added). The client method `getHumanStats(ruleset_id)` targets the documented aggregate shape at `GET /human/stats?ruleset_id=` so US-156's profile page has a stable seam; if the backend lands the route under a different path, only this one method changes.
- VITEST GOTCHA: a `vi.fn().mockResolvedValue(jsonResponse(...))` returns the SAME Response object every call — its body is single-use, so a test that calls fetch twice throws "Body is unusable". For multi-call tests use `mockImplementation(() => Promise.resolve(jsonResponse(...)))` (fresh body per call) or chained `mockResolvedValueOnce`.
- SVELTE-CHECK GOTCHA: a `let x: (() => void) | null = null` assigned ONLY inside a callback is narrowed back to `null` by svelte-check's control flow (calling `x?.()` errors "Type 'never' has no call signatures"). Hold the late-assigned callback in an object (`const pending = { reconnect: null as ... }`) so the type is not narrowed.
- Gates (all GREEN): ruff check ., ruff format --check . (406 files), mypy src tests (363 files), pytest -m "not integration" -> 2113 passed / 40 skipped; pnpm -C web/dashboard lint, check (0 errors), test (41 vitest), test:e2e (15 passed / 3 skipped Playwright).

## Codebase Patterns (append)
- Frontend human-session credential mode (US-153): the SvelteKit `PadrinoClient` carries TWO independent credentials — the spectator API key (Bearer header, read scope) and a human session (cookie). A human session is set http-only by the backend (guest quickplay / OAuth), so the client never holds the token; it only opts into `credentials:'include'` via `humanSession`/`setHumanSession`. Authenticated mutations go through a single private `mutate(method, path, body)` that JSON-serialises the body and routes errors through `PadrinoApiError`. SSE streams are consumed via a separate injectable `LiveClient` (EventSource factory) that reconnects BY SEQUENCE (re-open with ?after=cursor, drop frames <= cursor) — the same gap-free+dup-free contract the backend live-tail guarantees. Board/votes/chat derive from a PURE `playState.applyFrame` reducer fed ONLY by released frames; the runes `.svelte.ts` store is a thin shell so the logic is unit-tested without a runes test runtime.

## Codebase Patterns (append)
- Frontend in-game play surface (US-155): the /play/[gameId] page composes TWO SSE streams — the game-wide live-tail (released PUBLIC frames -> `createPlaySession` board/chat, reconnect-by-sequence) AND the seat-scoped observation snapshot (`seatObservationUrl`, US-136) for the caller's legal_actions + transport-only phase-deadline. Keep ALL load-bearing UI logic in a PURE helper module (playSurface.ts: status mapping, countdown bucketing, legal-action gating, sprite URL) and unit-test it without the runes runtime; the .svelte page is a thin reactive shell. NON-PRECISE countdown is a rule-7 requirement: bucket seconds-remaining into coarse labels (none/plenty/soon/ending) from an injected clock and render ONLY the bucket — never the exact seconds (a precise per-seat timer is a timing leak). The buffered chat composer maps the chat POST status (HELD/RELEASED/BLOCKED) to a pending/released/blocked badge; the feed is fed ONLY by released frames so the surface never shows an un-moderated message. E2E mocks SSE via page.route returning `text/event-stream` bodies (`id: <seq>\ndata: <json>\n\n`), aborting reconnects to avoid dup frames.

- web/dashboard/tests/e2e/reveal.spec.ts (new) — Playwright: guess-then-reveal + stats page
- ralph/prd.json (passes: true), ralph/progress.txt

What it does:
- /play/[gameId]/reveal: the spot-the-AI guess UI (per-seat HUMAN/AI toggle buttons + a
  SINGLE submit) is shown FIRST and GATES the disclosure of BOTH the viewer's own detection
  accuracy AND the canonical endgame reveal. After submit, the per-seat truth is shown
  (human/AI badge, role+faction, exact model, takeover provenance, themed sprite) + the
  accuracy banner. The viewer's own seat is excluded from the guess list (resolved from the
  observation snapshot pre-guess, confirmed by the scored result's guesser_public_id).
- /profile: a minimal stats page for a signed-in ACCOUNT (kind=='account'); a guest sees a
  sign-in prompt. Casual framing only — the rendered stats block contains NO elo/rating/
  leaderboard wording (asserted by the e2e). Reuses the existing client.getHumanStats /
  getHumanMe and the existing TS types.

Gates (all GREEN): ruff check ., ruff format --check . (406 files), mypy src tests (363
files), pytest -m "not integration" -> 2113 passed / 40 skipped; pnpm -C web/dashboard lint,
check (0 errors/0 warnings), test:e2e -> 20 passed / 3 skipped (visual snapshots) Playwright.

## Codebase Patterns (append)
- Gated guess-then-reveal (US-156): the reveal page reuses the EXISTING client methods
  (publicGameReveal US-143, submitTuringGuess/getTuringGuess US-144) — NO new client/type
  code was needed; the full EndgameReveal/SeatReveal/RevealModel/TuringGuessResult/SeatGuess
  types already shipped. The imitation-game hook is purely a frontend gate: `guessed` =
  `accuracy !== null`, and the {#if !guessed} branch shows the guess UI while the {:else}
  branch shows the accuracy + reveal board — so neither the per-seat truth nor the accuracy
  is rendered before submit. On mount the page calls getTuringGuess and treats a PadrinoApiError
  status===404 as the NORMAL pre-guess state (not an error) so a returning guesser sees the
  reveal immediately. The viewer's OWN seat (which a guesser never guesses) is resolved
  pre-guess from a single seatObservationUrl frame's `you.player_id` (the play-surface pattern)
  and post-guess from the scored result's `guesser_public_id`. E2E mocks /turing-guess for
  BOTH GET (404 before, 200 after) and POST (capturing the submitted guess map), /reveal,
  and a one-shot observation SSE; the stats spec mocks /human/me (kind=='account') + /human/stats
  and asserts the rendered block has no elo/rating/leaderboard substring (casual framing).

## 2026-06-20T23:55 PDT - US-189 (retry 2 fix)
- Adversarial verification caught a regression in the idempotency guard: `persist_pending_events` used a MAX-sequence threshold (`stored.sequence <= max_persisted_sequence`). In a human tick `run_tick` appends `ActionTimedOut` / `OutputInvalid` failure events at LOWER sequences WITHOUT co-committing them, then a chat-release / takeover co-commits its `content_ref` / `SeatTakenOver` row at a HIGHER sequence in the SAME tick. The max threshold then equalled the co-committed sequence, so the loop skipped the lower un-persisted failure rows — which are persisted nowhere else — and a rehydrate from `game_events` reconstructed a divergent state (the exact hard-rule-4 divergence the story set out to kill).
- Fix: replaced the MAX threshold with the EXACT set of already-persisted sequences. Added `events_repo.persisted_sequences_from(session, game_id, *, from_sequence)` returning `set[int]`. Extracted the loop body into module-level `game_runner._persist_pending_event_rows(persistence, event_log, log_before)` (the closure now delegates) so it skips ONLY sequences already committed and still persists every non-co-committed event below a co-committed row. Trimmed the now-misleading `max_persisted_sequence` docstring (kept the function; nothing else uses it but it stays a thin helper).
- Test: new `tests/runner/test_persist_pending_events_mixed_batch.py` builds a mixed batch (failure events at seq 0,1 NOT co-committed + a co-committed row pre-persisted at seq 2 via `_persist_stored_event`) and asserts EVERY event_log sequence has a matching `game_events` row with no duplicates; a second test asserts a full re-run over an already-mirrored batch is a no-op (no `uq_game_event_sequence` trip). Verified the old MAX logic would drop seq 0,1 (scratch check) so the test genuinely guards the regression.
- Files changed: `src/padrino/db/repositories/events.py`, `src/padrino/runner/game_runner.py`, `tests/runner/test_persist_pending_events_mixed_batch.py`, `ralph/progress.txt`.

## 2026-06-21T00:20 PDT - US-190
- Closed FINDING 2: the per-user daily inference-$ cap and the global cost breaker were plain SELECT-sum-vs-threshold reads (TOCTOU) — concurrent admissions all read sub-threshold spend and all passed, overshooting the $ budget. Separately every create/join/launch claimed a count slot that was NEVER tied to the resulting game/member, so an admitted-but-abandoned action permanently consumed a day-cap slot (self-DoS; cap counted ATTEMPTS not games).
- Atomic $ caps: new `human_inference_reservations` table (migration 0044, head 0043 -> 0044) models the remaining $ budget as finite discrete slots. `admit_human(...)` now claims a GLOBAL slot then a per-user (`scope_key=principal.hex`) slot atomically via `begin_nested()` + `uq_human_inference_reservation_slot` IntegrityError-retry; budget slots = `floor(budget / padrino_human_admission_inference_reserve_usd)` (new setting, default 0.5), already-charged spend implicitly fills the lowest slots (`ceil(spent/reserve)`). N concurrent admits can never exceed the slot count -> no overshoot. The breaker stays throttle-not-kill (it only gates new admissions; nothing boots an active game).

The slot allocator was reworked so a released slot frees its cap budget but keeps its physical index (`_next_free_index` picks the lowest index not physically present; cap = `implicit + len(live) >= cap`) — otherwise a re-claim would loop forever on the unique constraint.
- A per-call `_rollback_reservations()` DELETEs reservation rows already claimed when a later cap denies, so a denial leaks no held budget slice.
- Tests (tests/economics/test_human_cost_governance.py): N=10 concurrent admits under a 2-slot inference budget (file-backed SQLite) -> exactly 2 admitted, rest `daily_inference_cap_reached`; the same for the GLOBAL breaker with distinct principals; rollback proofs (no orphan reservations after an inference/count denial); aborted-create and aborted-join release-and-reuse proofs (a freed slot is reclaimable, exactly one LIVE count slot at a time). - Closed ROUND-2 FINDING 1 (CRITICAL): the chat-release replay-gap crash window. In a human DAY tick `run_human_tick` appends `ActionTimedOut`/`OutputInvalid` failure events to the in-memory `event_log` at sequence N (persisted nowhere yet); `release_chat` then runs in the SAME tick, co-committing a `content_ref` chat event at N+1 with its sidecar/hold write (own txn). `persist_pending_events(log_before)` only mirrored the lower N event AFTER the tick returned (game_runner.py:867), so a crash between the N+1 commit and that persist left `game_events` = `{N-1, N+1}` with N missing -> `replay_event_log` re-seals non-contiguously and raises `ReplayHashMismatchError` on `rehydrate_active_human_games`, permanently wedging the in-progress human game. US-189's persisted-set skip only helps if persist_pending_events actually runs.

- Closed ROUND-2 FINDING 5 (HIGH): migration 0045 unconditionally ran `op.create_index(..., unique=True)` on `leagues(ruleset_id) WHERE kind='HUMANS_INCLUDED'` with no preceding dedup. The pre-0045 `get_or_create_humans_included` (base d831d1f) was a bare read-then-create with no DB constraint, so a deployed DB could already hold duplicate HUMANS_INCLUDED leagues for the same `ruleset_id`. On such a DB, CREATE UNIQUE INDEX raises a duplicate-key IntegrityError and ABORTS the upgrade. The new savepoint-based recovery in leagues.py only prevents FUTURE dups; it never cleans up pre-existing ones.
- Fix (folded into 0045 IN PLACE - no new revision, head stays 0045 per AC2): `upgrade()` now runs `_dedup_humans_included_leagues(op.get_bind())` BEFORE creating the index. It selects all HUMANS_INCLUDED leagues, groups by `ruleset_id`, and for any group with >1 row keeps the earliest `(created_at, id)` keeper, repoints every dependent FK to the keeper, then deletes the losers - so the index creation always succeeds. Repointing covers ALL six tables with a FK to `leagues.id` via the fixed `_DEPENDENT_LEAGUE_FKS` allowlist (gauntlets, ratings, rating_events, human_rating, human_rating_event, lobbies), each guarded by `sa.inspect(bind).has_table(...)` so the same revision is safe regardless of which sibling tables already exist at run time. Portable raw-SQL UPDATE/DELETE via `sa.text` works identically on SQLite + Postgres. `downgrade()` unchanged.
- Tests (`tests/db/test_migration_0045_dedup.py`): `test_0045_dedups_duplicate_humans_leagues` upgrades to 0044, seeds two HUMANS_INCLUDED leagues for `mini7_v1` (distinct created_at) + a single `bench10_v1` league + a gauntlet pointing at the LOSER, then `command.upgrade(cfg, "0045")` MUST NOT raise; asserts exactly one league per ruleset_id, the earliest keeper survived, the gauntlet was repointed loser->keeper, and the unique index exists. `test_0045_clean_db_upgrades_normally` is the no-duplicates regression guard. `test_migrations_all_dialects` / `test_migrations` still pass.

## 2026-06-21T08:30 PDT - US-203
- Closed ROUND-2 FINDINGS 9 + 13 (LOW). (9) Multi-bucket rate-limit enforcement was record-then-decide per bucket: `_enforce_action_rate_limits`/`_enforce_chat_rate_limits` iterated (principal_key, game_phase_key) calling `record_request`, which INCREMENTS before returning a decision. So with per_game_phase(30) < per_principal(60), submits 31..60 in one phase 429'd on the phase bucket but had already burned a per-principal slot — over-consuming the seat's per-principal/minute budget across its OTHER games/phases. (13) Dashboard profile `pct()` did `Number(value)` and em-dashed on NaN; a core fraction-string like '2/3' (core/turing/scoring.py `_accuracy_string`) -> NaN -> em-dash if `detection_accuracy` ever arrives in that format.
- FIX (9) = peek-then-commit split, NOT bucket reordering. Added a non-incrementing `peek_request` to the `RateLimitStore` Protocol + both backends (`InMemoryRateLimitStore`: read current window count, no write; `DatabaseRateLimitStore`: `SELECT count` for the window row, no upsert, no eviction). Both enforcement helpers now PEEK every bucket first; only if every peek admits do they `record_request` ALL buckets. A later bucket's rejection never commits an earlier bucket's increment. Same pattern applied to both action and chat channels.
- FIX (13) = `pct()` parses a `'num/den'` ratio (regex `^(-?\d+)/(\d+)$`) into a percentage, still handles numeric/decimal-string inputs, and falls back to rendering the core string verbatim (mirrors the reveal-page verbatim-render fix from US-195) instead of an em-dash for any non-empty unparseable string; empty string still em-dashes.
- Tests: `tests/api/test_human_rate_limit_peek_commit.py` (NEW) - asserts a per-game/phase rejection does NOT increment the per-principal bucket for BOTH action and chat channels, plus the mirror (principal-cap rejection doesn't double-count the phase bucket). `tests/api/test_rate_limit_store.py` - peek-does-not-increment for InMemory + Database stores, peek reports full with retry_after. `web/dashboard/tests/e2e/reveal.spec.ts` - new profile test: `detection_accuracy: '2/3'` renders '67%', not an em-dash / NaN.

## 2026-06-21T10:25 PDT - US-206
- Closed ROUND-3 R3 (HIGH): US-197 moved takeover `apply_takeover` after the DB commit to prevent memory-ahead-of-DB corruption, but that left the opposite crash window. If the post-commit apply raised, `game_events` already held the `SeatTakenOver` row at sequence N while the long-lived in-memory `EventLog` did not, so the next tick could build another event at sequence N and collide on persist.

Non-contiguous or conflicting memory raises `TakeoverApplyRecoveryError` before any later event can be built at the colliding sequence. `SeatMultiplexAdapter.force_swap_seat` is the narrow DB-authoritative rebind used by this recovery path.

## 2026-06-22T16:03 PDT - US-233
- Added an explicit single-host restart-resume regression for a human-lane game
  stopped mid-`DAY_1_VOTE`: the test calls
  `rehydrate_active_human_games()`, resumes through `run_human_lane`, verifies
  the persisted phase/deadline, asserts the resumed tail chains from the
  previous head, and checks replayed terminal state equals the live game row.
- The regression asserts idempotent rehydration of the in-progress phase:
  `DAY_1_VOTE` has exactly one `PhaseStarted`, one `DayVoteResolved`, one
  `PhaseResolved`, and one vote submission per seat after resume.
- Single-host scope note: the human lane needs no distributed lease in this
  design. The worker heartbeat is a health signal, not a lease; reconnect-grace
  presence (`padrino_human_reconnect_grace_seconds`) is the only seat/game
  liveness mechanism, and distributed leasing / multi-host coordination remains
  explicitly out of scope.
- Test learning: a tight `run_human_lane(..., poll_interval_s=0.01)` heartbeat
  loop can contend with a real resumed game on the shared in-memory SQLite
  StaticPool and produce artificial persistence gaps. For restart-resume tests,
  wait on the executor and keep the poll interval long.
